Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, if he is given a well-made bandage, and it is worn for another 40 days; and have good rest, that he does not overexert himself and be careful of excessive drinking and eating, and of loud shouting; and when he has done this treatment, then is completely healed. de la routure dou ventre	Of the twisting of the belly

de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cauter called "point", and the cauter should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, and its weakness and virtue and location of twists and pain. If it is cured from the first cauter, good; if not, repeat another cauter on top of that one, for it is customary that it must change in the member closest to it, why you should do the cauters until the sickness is healed.
de meselerie	De meselerie ( likely a medical or surgical procedure)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The sick are helped sometimes by fire treatment with great aid, and just as much the disease that comes from putridity of bile and melancholy. So when you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will penetrate all of the patient, then do five fires on the head: one inside the head as far as possible, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the crown; and leave your hand so that the fire comes up to the bone, and so that the skin and the outermost layers come out in such a way that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize on the navel according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is scattered everywhere and it is clearly worsening, it is necessary that you cauterize with these fires on the head that we have said, and one fire near the navel, and two fires on the spine of the neck, and six fires on the spine of the back, and one large on the hip and one other below, and two on the shoulders; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the thigh, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the backside that you do not burn them; and never make a fire on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more fires I make, the more help and benefit it brings; and know that the sick do not feel pain during the fire, as the healthy ones do, because their body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary to have both large and small fires according to the members and joints, in such a way that you will find them in the ways of iron.
de enfleure	from swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes in any member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, but it is not cured, then the doctor makes cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be a little entering into the fat of the skin; then treat it with ointments until it is cured. And sometimes one makes a cautery and on the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if the swelling is removed; but however, one does not meddle with it unless he knows the members and the issues of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "ulcer" is inflamed, and no medicine can help it, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the amount of fat in the skin, until the white spot is removed, and its color changes; then treat it with a mixture of barley flour and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and vinegar of gall and vinegar of almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound as long as it is cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	Here's how to cure syphilis (chancre) by cauterization:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you see it arresting, if you cauterize it with the fire cautery that looks like .i. circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And yet wise men have said that one should make a cautery also in the middle of the chancre; and yet this seems to me not good, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen once; and the more direct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation which cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it takes long to heal, or because of the superfluity that it makes, or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has plenty of blood, or because of the time; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize it all around with many small cauterizations that are piercing; afterwards leave it thus. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the cauterization, then heat the cauterization until its form melts:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauterizations have pierced to the core, and be such cauterizations that the patient feels nothing outside, in such a way that the flow of the purulence is alleviated. Afterwards cure it until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by iron with fire
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than gangrene of a member, for it corrupts the members just like fire corrupts dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can suffer cauterization with fire, then heat the cauterizers with very hot iron, both small and large, according to what is needed at the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize all around until you have removed all the corruption, so that nothing remains of it except for what has been consumed. And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places some oil to broil them, so that the heat from the fire is removed and all the corruption.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	From boils which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	The boils that come to the feet often bring a disease called "cloves" according to our intention, and it is a large foul thing that hurts the foot. And there are two types of ulcers for this disease. It's either fire ulcer, or hot water ulcer. Fire ulcer is when you heat up one cauterizer like a blacksmith's pen, made of good iron to the size that can pierce the nail from all sides, and have subtle edges; then put it very hot on the clot, and turn your hand completely around the clot until it reaches the core of the clot; and let it be thus for three days until it starts to ooze pus; then make a poultice of bitter wild herbs crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the clot will fall off and be pulled out from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment melting fat as long as it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by boils on the body, and it often happens in hands and feet, it is necessary that you apply hot water cauterization; and it is in this manner: take a copper or iron canister, or a blacksmith's pen, and put it on the clot and the verrucas, that is to say, boils; and put the canister on so that it pierces all around, then add a little hot water, and hold your hand tightly, and press your hand while turning so that the edges of the canister come up to the root of the clot, and you find the hot water going deep enough to reach the root; and let the patient suffer the cauterization by the hot water for an hour; then leave it alone, and it will pull out all its roots. In this way do another one after another until you have extracted all those that are on the body, then cure the places with ointments that melt fat.
li cure dou trembler	It seems like there's a new text snippet provided.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some person trembles with cold or quartan fever or another thing, it is necessary that you make four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one on the hip, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; then he will let him shake, and quickly the health will depart from the disease of cold.
des pustules puans	boils that burst.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	At times appear on the body blisters or boils that burst forth from great corrupted matter. It is necessary when they first appear to make a cautery on each head of the boil: a subtle cautery made from the wood of myrtle, so that the point is seized with fire, or from the root of aristolochia longa, or from the lentil cautery. And at no time should one cauterize them when they first appear in this manner, so that they cannot grow further forward, but are broken off from the superfluities from which they come and are cured; but it is necessary that this be done after evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great discharges of blood come from the artery that is cut in the wound, or from the incision of the abscess, or from the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop them.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, if you hasten to put your finger's tip on the wound of the vein, and press down as much as the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips out; then put multiple small and large olive cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either great or small according to the wound and its place where the artery runs, and place the cautery on that vein which you hold with your finger, and keep the cautery there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts out again when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, then take promptly another of the cauters that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do these one after the other until the bleeding is stopped. And beware that you do not burn the nerve that lies nearby, and that no other malice comes upon the sick person. And know that when blood flows from an artery, it can not be well stopped in itself, especially if the artery is large, unless it is done by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not tied, or by a strong ligature with thread, or by medicines applied to which have the power to stop blood; and it should be bound and strained properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever reminds them of the dangers of tightly tying with a cloth or putting hot things on them, or other similar things, if they do not benefit them. (This sentence seems to be an aside, possibly written by a different author or added as a note.)
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have a surgeon or medicine present, they should put their finger's tip on the wound of the vein as we said, and press down well until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the hand, but moisten it with cold water often until it is very cold so that the bleeding is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make inquiries in advance for the cauters and medicines that they need.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all disease wherein it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or hot medicine, and the reasons and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I put that chapter at the head until now, and I shall go into this chapter by the same way so that what you want to find will be more easily found.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and therefore it is necessary to be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Because in the work of this chapter there are many times evacuation of blood when opening the vein, and to the incision above an abscess, and to the care of wounds, and to the extraction of arrows, and to the incision above a bone, and similar things; or there is doubt and fear, and death comes to many.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not take folly into account. For many ways of people come to cures. Some come in such a state with their disease that they will die easily due to the foolishness that is found in their disease, and the greatness of their malice; and these should be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among them are those who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is scornful. It is not necessary for you to agree with those who come to you who have this manner, but rather put more trust in your honor than in your gain, and do not act foolishly but wisely in what you are certain of, and from which you can take and receive praise; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your patients for whose salvation it will be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have ordered this chapter by chapters, dividing according to the chapter of burns, which I have divided from head to foot, for you will find it more easily that which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	two full waterheads
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes often to children at birth, and when the cord tightens too strongly around the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness occur in anyone but children, and with all those that I have seen it has been the cause of death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is not worth my while to continue working on these remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose ears were full of water, and the head was swelling each day to the point where it could no longer be sustained; and thought he was so sick that he would die, and this sickness is assembled under the bone above the forehead, between the eye and the bone; and the remedies are such that if the moisture is between the eye and the bone, and the swellings are small, you make a cut on top of the head through which the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the swelling is larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the signs that the corners of the head are open on each side, and the water spurts out when you press it with your hand from inside, and this is not a known condition: then you should make three cuts in the middle of the head, according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all of the moisture from outside. After that, bind up the cuts with cloths and powders, and apply vinegar and oil to them, and let them be in this state for five days; then untie them, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and also let the head strain freely, and give the patient dry food from broth as soon as the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you observe the position of the greatest part of the swelling and the gathering of the water; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes at the back, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut there where the swelling and the gathering of the water are most prominent, and incise according to what you can manage; but be careful not to cut the artery, lest a flood of blood ensue, causing the patient's death from bleeding and evacuation of moisture.

de la gresle	frostbite
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Often they come in the form of papers with something that looks like frostbite in its shape and hardness, and for this reason, this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of moist swellings on both sides of the paper above and below; the operation is as follows: be careful if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the cut wide, then peel off each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and close it; if you cannot close it without piercing the paper slightly, do not harm the patient at all; and if the wound is large, sew it up with a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do nothing forcibly, because ointments will restore it quickly and repair the skin.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending inside the ear towards the top part, then turn the paper around and take the grandine with tweezers, close it, and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it will not harm anything; and when the grandine has been closed, clean the wound with salt water, and cure the place where healthy skin is forming until the patient is healed.

des poilz des papieres	the hairs of paper

de la char qui vient en l’oil	This text appears to be a medical recipe or treatment from medieval France, likely written in Old French. The topic is "de la char qui vient en l'oil", which translates to "of the flesh that comes into the eye". The text describes an illness called "aleacrati" or ulceration of the eye, and provides a treatment plan involving cutting open the affected area, applying soothing substances, and taking precautions to prevent the condition from returning.

dou soudement de la papiere	Il semble que vous avez coupé votre phrase...

When this suture occurs in many people in the same way as the paper above is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move or do its natural operations, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and the stitches should be so fine that they are not too harsh or too rough, so that the patient cannot tolerate the stitches being too harsh and causing bleeding in the eye; and your incision, from which you will scrape off this assembled thing, should be done lightly, so that the paper regains its natural shape; and the entire assembled thing is cured, and sometimes in the eye there is a salty water and a sweet liquid and vinegar; then put between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put woolen cloth wetted with egg yolk on top of the eye; and after three days cease from using vinegar and things that are sours until they are healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is known that the corner of the eye is in two manners: it is nervous and resembles a hard, thick skin, and another which is not nervous but resembles white, frozen moisture, that when you touch it with an iron and try to scrape it with tweezers, you cannot; and both appearances begin near the large tear sac, and grows little by little until it covers the entire eye, sight, light, and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	It is known that the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your hands, then you open their eyelids. Lift the paper with your hand, then scrape the corner of the eye with tweezers from a small fold, and then take an iron needle, and insert one hair from a horse, or a cow, or a bull, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little bit and stick it into the corner of the eye, and pierce through the entire needle, and tie the corner of the eye with a thread and fasten it above; then scrape off all the hair from the side of the corner of the eye that is next to the tear sac and leave it until you reach the root of the lash with a very fine suture and small forces, and leave the natural tissue of the tear sac so that the incision does not bring the accustomed tears; and sometimes fasten only the corner of the eye with the iron needle and the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the remaining sutures from the smooth part which is the shape.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware that the suture does not touch the fatty tissue and break it, and that the tear sac is not pierced. And after the incision, pour a little bit of linen juice into the eye, and some litharge ointment, and let it be until the next day; then treat him with whatever is necessary until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the corner of the eye is not nervous and you cannot push in the needle, and the stitches cannot enter, this appearance of the corner of the eye is often cured with medications; and it grows like I have described in the division, and if you see it covering, you will work on the eye of the patient, and take a light, fine thread with a small knot according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift up the corner of the eye subtly, and if you see that it is not decreasing and the reason is pressing, then distill from your mouth into the eye a mixture made of litharge, red ointment, and linen juice, and close the eye until the next day; then start the other treatment according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no contradiction in the eye, like an apostume (a type of tumor or abscess), then let it drain, and first cure the hot aposteme until it is healed; then continue with the treatment as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the tear sac tissue is harming the eye with great damage, then suspend it with a stitch, and cut out a part of it but not all, so that there may be no flow of tears; then distill in the eye red ointment made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	...et qui se met sur l'œil. (And from the flesh which grows on the eyelid)
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Il est connu qu'à certains hommes une fois apparaît un charroux (une forme de cicatrice) rouge sur la paupière qui recouvre les papiers et se déforme au-dessus, ressemblant à une rose de balauste. Et le traitement consiste à faire que le malade mette son chef en ta main, puis tu ouvres les yeux, et tu attaches toute cette charroux avec des suture convenables à cela, et tu la soutiens à la force ; puis tu coupes la première char, et tu vas tout couper au rasoir jusqu'à la fin, et prends garde de ne pas blessé l'œil par l'opération. Et soit l'incision du spatumile que nous avons dit dans l'incision de l'ungule et les petites forces de quoi on ôte le sebel, comme la forme après ce chapitre en démontre.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Et quant la cicatrice (incision) est accomplie et que toute la charroux (tissu) soit ôtée, alors tu emploies du seil broiet (linon mouillé) ou tu distilles de la coliere rouge (un mélange médicinal corrosif) dans l'œil, et tu mets sur l'œil du coton avec abin d'œuf (une substance utilisée pour tamponner), si cela est assuré d'être une épistème chaude (une infection ou une éruption). Et s'il ne reste rien et que le saignement cesse, alors tu doutes que l'épistème soit chaude, alors laisse l'œil et cure l'épistème de choses apaisant l'épistème chaude ; puis reviens à ton opération (traitement) jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri, et ainsi feras-tu avec tous les chars qui sont ajoutés dans l'œil par cette semblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Mais il est toujours nécessaire d'observer la voie naturelle pour traiter chaque œil faible, et de ne pas recourir à des opérations de force (ovraige de fer) sauf en cas d'accident. Et il ne faut pas mettre ta main dans aucun de ces opérations tant que tu vois que le membre est souffrant du traitement.
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	These are the veins that are red and cover over the eye, and they tolerate with their activity and weaken the eye entirely. Therefore, at first you must look at the eye to see where the veins are, are they free from it, and is there no other illness outside of the veins; then treat the eye in this manner: command the patient to put his head into your hand, then suspend those veins by their whole length according to your wisdom, and let the needles be sharp and double in this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two needles, one by degree on either side in one piece according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then treat the eye with force those veins gently, and squeeze out the blood every hour after another, until you see the veins outside of the eye move; and be careful not to prick the eye at the points of the eyelids, and do this work at the hour of noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't miss what is outside of the veins; and when you have done this, if there is green or red pus remaining in the eye.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to clear everything out of the eye in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it sit for some days until the pains are soothed and you are assured that an abscess is hot, then resume the treatment in this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatments:
de la fistule de l’oil	Il semble que nous ayons terminé le texte. "De la fistule de l'oeil" pourrait être un titre ou une introduction à un autre traité médical, mais sans plus de contexte, il est difficile de savoir exactement ce que cela implique.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon's staff call these "arissati" fistules: when you cure them with a cauter and hot medicine as I have previously said, and they are not healed, then it is necessary to cut into the abscess above where it should die, and take out all of the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then raise it to all the instruments of which this is the shape; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron to a length of one head's width, and be sharpened like an awl as it is in the present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your thumbs and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is suppressed, and do this many times, then restore the place with medicinals to dry.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the place is healed, and flesh grows, and the body of the fistula is healed, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not re-appear and is no longer abscessed, and no bad accident comes, then know that it is healed; if not, there is no other treatment than to bring the fistula back to its natural place according to this shape: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and hot medicines, and when it is uncovered take one rod according to this shape, and the iron head be at three corners, and the handle should be thinned out up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the wound, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the rod completely until it pierces the bone and the sick person feels it through what the blood vessels do if they hold their hand over their fistula; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when flesh grows and hardens the place, then let the matter drain into the fistula; which is a lighter thing for the sick person.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the flow from the eye (or wound).
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are entirely opened wide and come out in their entirety, and there is no hindrance to vision or reduction, it is necessary that you instruct the patient; then bathe, then apply poultices or bandages with iron points to draw blood, then place on the eye a compress made of aloe, resin, incense, and sarsaparilla, and then bind the eye with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is such that you take cloth sufficiently soft, and double each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need, then bind it over with a firm cord, and repeat the poultices to draw blood without using iron points; then remove the poultices and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the compress becomes damp, it is necessary that you bind it tightly; then remove the compress after the day and the night, and if you see the eye repairing itself, it is good; if not, then repeat the dressing, cloths, compress, and poultices until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The final line of text can be translated as:
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee. de la bowe de l’oil	Of the back of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but the back of the eye that gathers in the eye, resembling a thread descending, and it's not a thread; and the way to recognize the treatment is as follows: you make the patient sit on a well-made and straight chair, then take their head between your hands from both sides, and pull until you see the back of the eye come up to your eyes; then be careful that it doesn't descend and be dislodged by light, and look at the things in front of them as they usually do. And if it doesn't descend, know that it's a thread, and if the descending movement of the back of the eye is not made in the way we said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine needle and sew on the corneal membrane one thread by the continuity of the conjunctive with the corneal membrane and the crown, until the back of the eye comes out; and when it has come out, distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or onion juice boiled with honey, then be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the threads of the eye (i.e., from cataracts)
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. And then carefully pierce the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put alum in it, as we have said; and when you finish the task, prepare the patient for a suitable bed, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be careful of all movements, take light food, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in that same dark house, test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put back the tie until the seventh day; and it is not necessary for you to perform these tasks during the treatment or after the incision now, but you must speed them up, because the swelling rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess forms in the eye, have it untied before the seventh day, and turn it towards what soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, release the eyelid and put a dressing on its face, i.e. a patch to cover for one day, and keep it in that dark house. And then go out of the house slowly and carefully, and change back into your clothes; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Iberian Peninsula (or Spain), who told us that in their peaceful lands they used to perform an operation called "almagda" perforation, where they would let out the abscess. However, I never saw anyone doing this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it's a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the shapes of ague, because one who does not know them sees them; and they are of proper silver:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are from the same subtlety, and their tails in three angles of ague.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the skin
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At times there appear on the skin flesh-like substances that are various and for which it happens that some resemble scorpions at their feet; and if one of these appears with flesh colored to be flecked with red color, or has pale colored flesh. In that one of these fleshes that is pale and not flecked, you must have the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the oil onto those fleshs, and chase them further away; then take what you can hold in the sharp pointed spatula from one side, as long as you know that flesh is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be removed, then open it with all the sharp pointed instruments lightly, until nothing remains; and if the abscess or swelling does not burst on its own, or if the suppuration is such as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize them so that the pain is stifled and all the flesh is removed, then pour either oil, vinegar, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the swelling opens and comes to just below the mouth, know that it is healed; and if the swelling does not break open as it should, know that there is flesh born in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach: then it is necessary that you put one thread of linen into it, a little thicker than a woman's thumb, with about half an inch between each node; and give the patient the ends of the thread to bite on as much power as he can muster, and pull gently until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times children do this in school, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then take the end that comes out of the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and pull them apart while holding onto the thread in the middle. Do this until you know that the nodes have corrupted the flesh, then pull out the thread, bleed the patient, and wet the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back into the swelling as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that is remaining of flesh; and then put a cloth on the swelling for several days until it is healed, and if it needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which one distills the oils and medicines onto the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a candlestick, and lead in the same way; and if you see that you need to make a closed candlestick, then do so, and have the instruments filled to purify the head; and have one handle at the top to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	It seems like this is just a phrase, possibly indicating the end of a recipe or a chapter, with the translation being:
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises in the head of the neck a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large over time, so that it is visible to the eye; and therefore you must cut it out at the beginning, and remove all flesh, then put on it the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it out until it is large, beware if it has become hard, with foul color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron for it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut into it once, great mischief comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of pure touch, not at all with foul color, and you see that one can cut it out entirely, then the patient will be empty and the cut sensible without fear, and cure the place of things constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the abscess is cut out and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous joints, it is beneficial for few things, more so than in some men. It therefore happens that when this occurs in anyone, you should look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a suture, then cure until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from each other on one side and the other, you should scrape away all the parts of their sore until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and bind them, and sprinkle on top powder of dragon's blood and frankincense broth; and put on top of the powders a piece of a binding plaster or another binding plaster, and leave it until it is set by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the suture is that you assemble the solution with either needles or thread, just as we have said in the suturing of the belly wound.
des apostemes des levres	Les apotèmes des lèvres sont une maladie grave qui peut affecter les lèvres et la bouche. D'après le texte médical médiéval, les apotèmes des lèvres pourraient être traités de plusieurs manières, notamment en utilisant des poudres et des huiles pour aider à cicatriser les plaies et à prévenir l'infection.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	A multitude of people have ulcers inside their lips that are hard and similar to grains of sesame seeds, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, incise each node, and take it with forceps and cut in each part; then fill the wound afterwards with vinegar that has been boiled, until the blood is stopped; and then apply oil of asclepius, and cure the wound with things that are dry until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there arises on the gums a lump of flesh that the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary to hold it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let the vein or blood run; then put vinegar broth, or other restraining and drying powders, on the wound; and if that flesh returns after incision, and many times occurs, then cut it again and cauterize: if it does not return after cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	At times they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes they are black and green and worm-eaten, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling; if it is necessary you must have the sick person sit between your hands, and his clothes be in your sight, and remove the teeth or scabs as they appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and greenish hue, and yellowing and other blemishes, until they are removed; and if one removes what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, then you start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to how the work shows, because the rasers used to remove teeth from outside the mouth have other forms than those used to remove them between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as possible before pulling it, because this should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance, and one must have no excuse to pull it. (Note: "raier" here means "to pull out or extract", and "dou raier" means "without an excuse")
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then, when the patient is forced to have it pulled out, you must be certain of the healthy tooth. Many times the pain has fooled the patient, and they think it's the good tooth, and they've had the good tooth pulled out; and yet the pain doesn't depart, as long as the bad tooth remains, because we've already done that to these patients. And when you're well certain of the healthy tooth, then you must scrape around the tooth on all sides, making it very hard to protect the gum in all places; then move it with your hands or thin pincers at the first point and second point, until it's well extracted, then tighten the pincers. And the patient's clothes should be in your sight between your knees, and you must hold them tight so that they don't move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it doesn't fall out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each side, then move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced or crushed, you must fill it with cotton or wool where the holes are; and when you extract the tooth carefully with pincers, so that it doesn't break when straining; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you don't break it and leave a piece of it behind, which will cause the patient to suffer even more pain from the root, greater than the first. And beware that you don't do as ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and boldness break the bone sometimes and don't bring about what we have told; but instead they often bring about great suffering through the roots that remain or the bone they break, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, vinegar, and salt; and if a scab forms there, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if this doesn't help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the extractors, through which one moves the teeth first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should have large limbs that do not bend when pulled, and be made of well-made iron, and have teeth to keep them from slipping.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at the pull, you should put a wet cotton on top of the place, i.e. for one or two days, as long as the place is softened, then insert the pincers that are called "algefri", through which the nerves seem to be like the beak of a vulture; and they should be made inside as well as a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and insert the instrument that is called "althali", i.e. palanque, through which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through this one, it's good; if not, you help with all the extractors, through which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it helps with this instrument that has two handles, through which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fastenings which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems a pair of great pincers, whose form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is for when it cannot break; and know that many instruments of dens are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise and subtle master finds his own instrument by himself according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancient did not teach a tool for their diversity and I do not break the cartilage or the other bones if it can be helped, so I look for the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and help from gestures, of what this is the form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be big and hold well in order to hold the bone so it does not slip, but rather can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicine suitable for this, and if there is rotting inside the bone, and it is small, so restore all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural body and their shape is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the tooth and is not in its right place and cannot be filed or smoothed: then file it; and if it is sharp with the tooth, take this instrument which is of this form, and resembles a small beak, and is made of iron with an edge like a saw.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, use this file with a similar shape to this form.
