et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth short and short in hand lightly, so that it does not move until it is sharp; then smooth it out completely to no roughness, and if the tooth is too pointed and hurts the tongue, you need to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth decay (lochent) or rot (porriture).
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth decay, either by impact or falling, and the disease cannot be pressed back to where it came from without breaking through, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, but that doesn't work; then they need to be restrained with a gold wire. The silver wire becomes green and decays, but gold never changes; and the wire should be of medium thickness or too thin or too thick, according to the space between the teeth; and if you want to align the teeth, take the wire and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the wires between the misaligned teeth, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then start again with the covering up to the part where you started, and pull gently and subtly, until it doesn't move anymore; and make sure the wire is tied at the root of the tooth so that it can't escape. Then bend the wires of the wire into a pair of pliers, assemble them, and insert them between the healthy teeth, and place them in such a way that they don't hurt the tongue; then leave them there tightly until they can stay, and if they come loose or the wire breaks, then tighten it with another wire. If they remain and serve like that for all their time, this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two misaligned ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then place it back in its proper position, fresh and fresh, as we have said; and don't interfere with it unless you are wise and patient, and sometimes make a shape like that of an ivory tooth, and place it in the position where the defect is, and tighten it as we have said, and let it stay and serve like this for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to remove the thread from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this thread comes from under the tongue naturally when we are born, or by accident of a wound that has healed; and the operation is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, with their head in your own healthy one, and lift up the tongue; then remove the nervous thread with a large clamp, so that the tongue is detached from its seat, and if there is hardness or numbness, which comes from a sudden wound, you put an incision and clamp it tightly on both sides of the thread; and make sure the opening is not too deep, lest the artery under it be damaged. And when you have done this, then lift up the head with a rose-colored cloth and oil, or cold water, and place a linen bandage over the tongue; and let the patient clean the area every night, so that the wound does not heal.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer is of foul color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining to gangrene, and there is moisture, throw in vinegar, and make from a subtle spatula, and free it from one part and the other; and if the blood seeps into your work, put on vitriol plaster so that it is dried, then return to your work until you have extracted all pus; then lift the affected area of linen and cloth, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come from within the throat swellings which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard swelling of small size and foul color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron for its bleeding; but let it stay until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break off by itself. And if it is white in color and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cut it, but first examine whether the swelling has cooled down and is calmed. Then sit the patient before the sun, and your hands be clean, and open the mouth and take the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue below all the instrument, which is its shape; and it should be of silver or fine bronze as thin as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue down onto this instrument, and you will see the swelling, then take a needle and push it into the almond, and pull it out through above as far as your finger; and do not touch anything with the cloth, then cut it with the instrument, which is its shape, resembling a forceps. And although the handles are bent and one end meets the other, and are very sharp, and made of iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, cut it with forceps, which is its shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And they should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have cut out one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and cold water, and vinegar, and if there is bleeding from the wound, gargle the patient with water or cooked apple cores or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops. Then cure the patient until they are healed. And sometimes other swellings come up in the throat besides the two almonds, then cut them out in the same way as the two almonds were.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed in the back of her throat, which was pressing against the airway. It was so swollen that it had pushed two teeth out on either side, and she couldn't breathe or eat because it had blocked the passage. If she had stayed like that for just one day or two, she would have died.
de l’uve	of the liver
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the abscess is located on the liver and it swells and becomes long, it's called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and rounded, it's called an "abscess". When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the incision does not help, and you see that the abscess has become smaller and more subtle, then you should excise it; and one that is rounded and not long, and is sanguine or of a bloody color or black, then you should avoid making an incision on it. For there is great danger for the patient. So, when you see it, according to the shape I have described, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the abscess and draw out the pus, and excise it with one or two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds. And you must not excise more than the superfluous matter that is beyond the natural term; for if you excise more, you will cause pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said about the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of being cut, then you should use a trick at the cauterization on them without fear. And the way of cauterizing is very sharp; and it's that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses the tongue with the instrument that we mentioned or read about in the chapter of cauterizing, and mix with live water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and insert the handle of this instrument, which is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Je suis désolé, mais il semble que le texte contienne des erreurs ou des incohérences. Je vais essayer de traduire le reste du texte et vous donner une idée générale de son contenu.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more sure than incision or cautery; if it is cured through fumigation in this manner: take calaminth and yarrow and origanum and rue and chamomile and balm and similar herbs, and gather all of them together into one pot, and I put ashes in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument, a spade, according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and have one of the keys inserted in the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is numbified; after that repeat it often, until the eye dries, and take care that you do not do this at the beginning of the hot aposteme's coming, because many things happen then; and do not do this until the declination of the hot aposteme. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put inside the head one shard of eggshell, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot; for the shard of eggshell does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and it is a good cure together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	It often helps to insert a needle into the throat or spine of fish, or something else; so it is necessary that you try to see what can be seen, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you see movements in the thing; and if something does not appear and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit when the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of charcoal, or a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then have it swallowed; and when it comes up, it will be stuck, and you will pull it out; and if it does not come out according to what we said, take an instrument made of lead in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised upwards. Be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything go wrong, nor push the bone inside; and it is better if the patient puts the instrument in themselves, so that they know whether the thing is coming out or not. If they put it down, or pull it back up to the instrument with equal force, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	From the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	There is no medicine for blood from the throat, as I said in the division, by medical treatment; and when it does not help, then look into the patient's throat with sunlight; then press the tongue onto the instrument that I told you to. And if you see the blood, cut it off completely, i.e., a little less than an inch, or with fine tweezers that are good for this purpose. And if they are not effective, take a hair rope and put it into the patient's throat; then insert a hot iron at the top of the rope, and do this often. And if the patient is vomiting water all day, then take a full vial of cold water, open the mouth, and spit out in front of swallowing, and move it to his hand often; and as soon as the blood senses the water, it will flow.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it doesn't flow as we said, then suffumigate the patient with asefetide at the instrument that I told you about in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will flow soon. The manner of the fumigation is that you take one pot where there are glowing coals, and let the cover be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and on those holes put the instrument; then throw your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the end of the rope in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that no smoke comes out, but rather goes up to the blood; and now the blood will flow, and if it doesn't flow, then repeat the fumigation many times. And let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and not drink water; and then it is necessary for the blood to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	Je suis désolé, mais je n'ai pas compris la dernière partie de votre texte. Votre texte semble être écrit en ancien français, qui est une langue d'origine médiévale parlée principalement en France du XIIe au XVe siècle. Je vais faire de mon mieux pour traduire et comprendre le sens de ce qui suit.
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many forms of abscesses, as can be seen from the memory that comes later in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is itself, and due to moisture. And the second way is because of the place where it is on the body. For the abscess of the head is different from that of the fundament, and the abscess of the fatty part is different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in its work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if it is an abscess that should not be pierced until the swelling is dead according to its completion; and there are those such as it is necessary to pierce when they are thick, and do not die according to their completion, like an abscess that comes near joints. For when an abscess comes near a joint, and one leaves it so long that it becomes rotten around it, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupted, causing contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the fundament, then if one pierces it while it is still fresh; and it is not necessary to pierce an abscess that has become thick without being digested, unless it is that which is near the fundament, so that it does not become rotten inside and be prolonged, and come to fistula; and it cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the work of piercing an abscess that has become dead according to its completion, and it is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and trembling and hardening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the perforation in a place more dependent on the abscess, where it opens most easily; and the length of the perforation should be according to the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these swellings, pierce the affected member. And when an abscess is located in a fatty place, it is worth noting that you should leave the perforation until it is fully digested and confirmed; as we have said. For if you puncture before this, you will cause the body to become infected with venom from there, and be full of foul matter; and by chance harden the lips and the deepest part of it. And for any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what is needed by the member; and you must bring small abscesses to small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many slits according to the similarity of the size of the abscess. And for those abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it has become like a cloth, and is softened, then it is worth noting that you should do as one does with infants: and for those that are slit into three angles, and for those that have the core covered like a myrtle leaf, as abscesses of the kidneys; and for those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those that do not have a head, as soft superficial abscesses, it is necessary to pierce them completely. And when the abscess is large and has thickened with a great tumor, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the tumor at once, but take out part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then take out nothing more from there; do this several times in turns, as long as the tumor comes out entirely. Especially if the patient is weak or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit. For the spirit may shake at some point with the exit of the tumor, that by chance kill the patient, and you will not be aware of it. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, flush the wound, and look if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a plain cut, bring linen or old cotton tents; and if it's a large abscess, and there are many punctures, it is necessary that you tie one tent to each other; and if you have removed part of the skin, and wrapped around it, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or rags of linen threads moistened, and bind until the third day; then remove and cure with ointment as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound becomes inflamed with blood, bring cold and bitter vinegar, and a damp cloth, and apply it to the place where the wound is bleeding several times. And if the inflammation of the wound persists, bring governance and care, and the powders that I said in this book are good for hot wounds, and if it's in summer, and the place or the abscess is very swollen, it is necessary to put on wet tents and drapes in wine and hot oil; and if it's in winter, and the place is fleshy, it is necessary to put on wet drapes in vinegar and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and flush and cure it, as it is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	It seems that this text is a medieval medical treatise, likely written in French. The author is summarizing the general principles of treating abscesses (apostemes) and providing guidance on how to proceed with treatment.
des soros	Of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	When small swellings come to the head, they are like small blisters, and are in the shape of a spider's web, just like the threads from a hen's nest, and there are many similarities. There are some that are fat and moist like poults; and some that are hard and stony to cut, and I have no doubt that the artery makes them contrary. And the treatment for cutting is that you must try all instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which their shape comes next. For if they contain moisture, you do it over a long time. And when the moisture is drained out, you dry up without leaving any skin on it because it will come back again when you leave anything; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; otherwise in water and linen, and bandage the wound, and let it be just until the next day; and these will run those that are left from last night. And then start the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, as long as you know well that there is no more left from last night; then cure the wound with ointment as suitable, so it becomes healed. And if the blisters hold one night fat, cut them according to this form, over a long time; and throw away your needles, and scrape off all of its parts, and put all your treatment to squeeze out the juice where it lies; and if the artery makes you contrary, do what I told you afterwards. And so also do with the blisters if they are stony, and hard to cut, and to cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the treatment for the stony and moist blisters on the head is lighter, because they are full of blood. And if you have some of these blisters or on the head where there is no moisture, and among those was one blister that I carved on an old woman's head; and I found the blister just like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had taken any, he would have made a wound as much as of a stone. And for other blisters coming from the head, except those which come to children's heads and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at most dependent on where it needs to come out the bowstring; and cure them as they deserve.
des scrophules	Of the scrofulas.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Scrofulas often occur on the neck and under the armpits, and sometimes elsewhere in the body. And each scrophula is properly contained within its own coat, just like the boil and the swelling of the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrofulas. There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant and do not want to be cured. In the one you see with good disposition towards treatment, and is similar in color to the skin, and moves freely from each part and is not inflamed at the nape of the neck or at the artery or at the duct, and is not deep; then it is necessary that you cut it above, and scrape off every part, and apply the two lips of the cautery if you need them, as we have said about the swellings of the head. And be careful not to cut the nerve or the vein, nor should there be a scar or an incision, so that the hands may escape, and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut something that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not stop bleeding, then put vitriol powder in the wound to coagulate the blood and close the wound. Leave it like that until the swelling is calmed down and the wound becomes soft and begins to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, completing it as needed; then check if there are any small scrofulas left, cut them out and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrophula, do not need to cut out that scrophula from its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang loose without harming; then cover the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire scrophula, it is necessary that you close and sew up the two lips of the wound now, since there will be no superfluous tissue left due to the size of the scrophula. It is necessary that you aim to cut out its root, and pull tight, and then sew it as we have said. Those scrofulas that contain superfluous tissue, pierce them where they are most inflamed; and pierce them similarly to the one mentioned earlier, hanging down, then apply tents with ointment and like substances, so that what remains of the corruption will be corrupted; and when the wound is thoroughly cleaned, cure it with ointment dripping fat meat, until it is healed.
de squinance	It looks like we've reached the end of this text snippet! "De squinance" doesn't seem to be a meaningful phrase in English, but I think you might be referencing the fact that we're done with the medieval medical text excerpt.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw it done in our land, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have swooned, the incision of the throat called "epiglottis" should be made; and this should not be done by them because all the veins and the pulse of the sick person are warm at the mouth, or in the throat, or in both cheeks.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pulse, it must be cut through the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It must then be done when we want to cut the epiglottis that we cut it under three or four circles or a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the size of the incision of the scissors, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those things are convenient to the cutting of the epiglottis that there is no flesh and the blood vessels are long and stretched out.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is timid, it should be that he stretches out the skin of the throat to the whole length, then cuts through the skin as far as the channel; and stops up the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut with the scissors, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein in the channel which sprouts forth through the cut that is broken, and by the failure of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a piece (of time).
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which we doubt the strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound in the skin and sew it all up except for the cartilage; then administer medicine that causes flesh to grow, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	I beg you, do not perform this operation until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the pulse has failed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut out the epiglottis in order that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I see a young lady take .i. (that is) a dagger, and stick it in her throat, and cut out part of the channels under the tongue;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found that the blood was issuing from it, and I realized that she had not cut very deeply or caused much damage except in the throat, and the vein had come out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and cured her so that she was sound.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it did not harm the young lady except that she became hoarse from speaking, and returned to her normal state afterwards.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I said that in cutting the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This tumor is called an "umbilicus of the throat", and it is a great tumor in the color of jet, and it occurs very often in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two manners, of which one resembles a fatty lump, and the other manner resembles a tumor that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not seem good to operate on one that is small, and I prove and examine with all the instruments.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it to be just like a lump of fat, and it cannot move in any way, then cut it out, just as one cuts out fatty lumps, and treat the wound with all your care, if there is none.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and examine well throughout, and cure it as it needs to be, until it is perfectly sound.
des nous	of the fatty lumps
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of fatty lumps, which I will describe to you all their likenesses.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now it is fitting that I tell you the entire difference between a lump and an abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, holding heat until the bubbling has passed, and the corruption has been completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Unlike a lump, an abscess has neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains a pus-filled sac that is its own pouch, and is of the same color as the flesh, and begins like a jet-black liquid, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two likenesses, either fatty or moist, and of many colors, as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the lump, that you examine and investigate it first with all the instruments called "entromiçoires", according to what its form may be, whether chaptered or otherwise.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of investigating the fatty lumps is that you take or make the most moist part that you find in the lump, and turn your two probes back and forth, until you know that the instruments have pierced to the core, then according to the size of the lump.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then draw out the probe, and be careful about what comes out with it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moist pus comes out, whether of a certain color, then do with it as I said for the other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the probe no moist pus comes out, then know that it is fatty, so do with it thus: cut it in cross, and take it up with pincers, and scrape it lightly from each part, and then apply the poultice to where you will treat the lump, that you may dress it sound with the ointment.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot cure it by dressing, then cut it out in pieces, so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return the lump many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there remains a small piece and the pain does not subside, then apply a poultice to the wound with sharp corrosive powders, and bind the wound tight, and put on cooling things for the hot abscess, and cure it with other remedies until it is sound.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the lump is large, then cut off both edges of the wound, and cure it with those things that corrupt flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is so situated that it would be contrary to you or another to cut into it quickly, then apply a poultice of vitriol paste, and leave it for two or three days until the wound purifies, and lets the bubbling of the blood subside; then come back to cut out what remains of the lump.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold here the forms of the probes entromissoires, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and among them are three squares called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and among them are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to investigate the abscesses of fistulae.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one cuts out scrofulae, and are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and among them are those that are yellowish in value, and are most proven to be used for investigating the pustules of fistulae.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the orifices.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the lancets are of many likenesses, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are lancets that have two pustules in three ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are lancets that have three pustules, and they also come in three ways; and there are lancets that have two pustules, and lancets with a single pustule, and they all come in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The handle of these lancets are pointed, and among them there are some that do not cut at all on one side, from which one scrapes the lumps, so that they may not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and among these probes are the allemeles answered in strings, so that the sick person may not feel them when opening the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see here.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them at all on healthy skin, such as legs, arms, shoulders, and in similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling an iron for scraping abscesses, in this shape, with which one stops the bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes put at the place where healthy flesh comes together with veins and arteries, and they are cut in this large shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of certain men become inflamed when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like the breasts of a woman.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain ugly and inflamed, and if one wants to cure them, it is necessary to scrape according to this shape of the line b from point g:.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat and apply the wound with medicinal things that corrupt flesh, then sew up the two edges of the wound tightly, and cure it until it is sound.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast droops downward and is deformed because of its size, like in women, then make two small incisions above it, through two similar separations.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is joined to the other at the end of each one, so that the longer line contains the shorter one according to this shape, from line b to line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and put in everything that we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, until it is sound.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not sound, or the incision has not been completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the clotting of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until the remaining flesh and fat are consumed, then cure it until it is sound.
des apostemes des asselles	The abscesses of the armpits.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These swellings that come under the armpits are ways of hard scrofula or there is a rib; and among them there is one that contains moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those which contain moisture then should be cut according to this shape, from line B down to line G.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the swelling on the aposteme is all empty, then apply ointment to the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and dress with ointment as needed until they are healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the swelling is of the likeness of scrofula, then treat it as we have said in the cuts of scrofula, and if the wound swells again, apply cauterize as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn shut, then many times swellings come and he also has his vein swollen and swollen.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the swelling runs long in depth.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your hands, you feel i.e. stiffness; and when it is due to the vein, then there are rednesses on the outside appearing.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cut this swelling, and even more so when it is under the armpits and shoulders and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to shun the treatment of iron, and likewise for that which is at the head, it is also necessary to shun it, and in that which is due to the swelling of the artery make a cut over the long skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the wound with needles and separate beautifully the artery from its threads, until it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle under the artery and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temple.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then stitch the loop that is between the two threads with an introducer so that the skin comes out from it, and have the swelling come apart.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that we mentioned earlier to prevent swelling, until the stitches come undone.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with ointment suitable for this, until they are healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the swelling is due to the wound of the vein, it is necessary that you mark with your hand whatever you can remove from the swelling all over the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the mark you have on your hand and make it pierce through, and there will be one double thread, so that you can pull it out from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the swelling, just as I have told you, or tie one of its parts to the two knots of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will come out, then rebend another needle along all of the thread under the entire swelling at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the swelling until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the skin and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a warm cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply treatments of liniments and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, as abscesses come in the arteries and veins, abscesses also come on the nerves when they are inflamed, or from too great labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these things happen more often in the joints and hands and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and it is in many dispositions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one tightens it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it can move freely in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, up or down, and that which is in the joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps there would be contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who has it on the head or forehead, splits the skin on the suture.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, one takes hold of it with tweezers and cuts out its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is great, one suspends the abscess with thread, and scrapes it, then cuts out and sews up the wound to the suture, and cures him until he is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging ulcers
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it comes in the stomach and not elsewhere in the belly, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to fungi, and it has a subtle root and a large head; and there are small ones and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen one man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a small root, and were already split open, and were always moistening.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them out and found that one weighed 28 ounces, and the other 5 pounds, and the work of cutting in the incision is such that you look to see if the patient's flesh is moist, and the color of the fungus is white and moist and with a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if he cuts them out with a sharp instrument, and the cautery is being done in your presence by the fire. For when cutting comes there are often too great discharges of blood, and if the bleeding does not stop, then you must hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient shivering and fearful of the incision with iron, then take one thread of flax well made, and tie the fungus as we have said, and let it be for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not stop restraining the thread of flax until he cuts out the fungus, and let him sense that it was a good job; and if the roots are thick, have him be afraid to cut into himself in the belly, but you can well cut half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize him so that it does not return; then heal the wound, and be careful not to cut out the fungus which is of foul color and poor sense and with milk-colored sap.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an infected abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancre later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the blister bursts open.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the blister comes from a burn wound or an opening in the skin, and it is on the stomach and contains some blisters, as it does in other injuries, or blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is ahead, or by inflammation;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the wound of the skin and from the opening of the blister, then the color of the blisters is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the opening of the intestine, then it is even more varied, and when you press it with your fingers it bulges back out, and then returns, and perhaps it will close, and swells greatly at the entrance of the wound and for great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is from moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, not constrained; and if it is from blood, then it opens by these signs the blisters large and hard, and are stuck together in a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is from inflammation, then it is soft to the touch, and the signs are that you look whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery, or a vein, or inflammation.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If it's true that you should leave the wound alone. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on blisters, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, then it's fitting that you command the sick person to loosen their stool and be extended straight out, then sign on the entire length of the belly. ( likely a medical notation)
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command them to lie down soon between your hands.
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have marked with a spatula,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then take half of the poultice and apply it to the entire large incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it firmly with a strong thread or a cord of firm silk, and let the dressings be fastened.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work the other half of the poultice spread over the bandage, and insert your index finger, and push back the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught from the bandage, then unfasten it, and push the intestine to the outside of the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the haemorrhage, then take hold of the incision and remove the superfluity.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery makes against it, or the vein, then go around it gently, then come back to your work and take two needles, and insert two thin threads, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you make pierced;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then stretch the poultice over the needles in four places, and if you see it, take out the needles, and let it stay as long as it will stick, and let the dead flesh come off by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you can cut it when it has softened and stuck, then dress it with what is needed, and take care of the poultice as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and clean out the blood or moisture you find, then dress the place with what is needed, and sew up the wound.
dou chancre	Il semble que nous sommes arrivés à la fin de cette section sur les soins médicaux. Les instructions qui suivent semblent traiter du traitement d'un chancre (probablement une ancienne désignation pour un ulcère ou une maladie infectieuse). Voulez-vous continuer à lire ces instructions ?
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	Il semble que nous sommes en train de lire une section sur les soins médicaux pour un chancre. Les instructions qui suivent semblent être un avertissement quant à la gravité du traitement et à l'importance d'une grande précaution.
