Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not further than as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it be according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easily set right.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come further than as we have said, then take aloes, and oil of sassafras, and melted gum, and grind everything together in one mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put the essence of woman inside it and on top of this ointment.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in warm water until under the ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened underneath, make her a collar of myrrh and put it under, and let her leave it for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a stool, then make her stutter and hold her mouth and nose, and press her belly lightly, for the child is jumping now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child between her legs.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then take the cord (umbilical cord) with both hands little by little.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then bind it on its neck, and let the feet hang down, and lay it on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold its hands little by little, and then take the hands up to the belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until she is ready to go downstairs.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take its feet and shape them well, then shape the belly up, then insert your hands.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and push the child little by little, and command the woman to take hold until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child who comes out with one hand open, stretching (or: extending).
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is good to pull back the hand.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman get up and go (away from the bed).
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot get up, then make her lie on a bed, and draw out her legs well.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then bring the ointment that I have recounted.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a stool, and try to pull back the hand again.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and push the child according to its natural form, and make her stutter, and command that she hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child around its neck, and having spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is good that the cord takes hold of its hand, then turn it little by little, and push it gently.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal (in length), put on the natural ointment of aloes and oil, as we have said, then command that she move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make her sit on a stool, and command that she hold on, and make her stutter.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	from the same manner for all the afterbirth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes out in this way to all the afterbirth, cut the afterbirth at your finger's length, until the moistors are empty.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child is hanging from its face and neck, cut off the afterbirth at the mouth, so that it will not be retained, and kill the afterbirth.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then insert the child inside, as far as it is necessary, and command the woman to hold on once.
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	the issue of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born together, and sometimes they are three or four in a single birth; and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two of them are a strange thing, and do not live if there is no name (i.e., if one of the twins does not have a proper name).
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiple, and are divided by the navel string which separates them, which is tied to the mouth (i.e., of the womb).
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out just naturally like all of us do, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out quickly, then take care of them as we have said, and be sure the cord is subtle, and do what she does soon and easily.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and act just as one would in case of a normal birth to their salvation.
de plusors enfans	of more children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb to be one, or two, or three, or four, or five, or six, or seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all fully formed as an infant by the measure of the wise God.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the cord knows everything about this, because perhaps such a thing happens to her too.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	then act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	the stillborn child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you are treating the woman for a stillborn child or one that has died in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to intervene with your hands.
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is good that you know whether the woman has a healthy constitution, and has not had accidents or fears of death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is good that the woman be supine on her back, and her chin inclined downwards, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the attendant should grasp the navel string at two parts, or tie it to the bed so that she is not handled in lowering the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then wipe the mouth of the womb with moistened oils mixed with aloes and fenugreek and flaxseed oil, then anoint the hands of the attendant with these oils and ointments.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then insert them into the womb gently, then take one linen or another cloth that is suitable for this purpose.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and be careful if the child is wrapped up so that it comes out on its head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if you place the cloths in their own mouth or neck or face or palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the sides.
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on the feet, then place a cloth or bandage and sew it to the opposite side.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that you tie the cloth to her right hand and place the cord between her left hands' shoulders, and insert it into any of those places we have mentioned, until the thing comes out empty.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the cloth.
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then tie it against another cloth, or a third one if you need it, so that the extraction is equal.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch them evenly by moving from one side to the other, so that it may come out easily, and the cloths should be torn so as to hold tight, as is the shape.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if there remains a part, then anoint the attendant's shoulders with oil and insert them into that part, and pull on the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains nothing, then place this cloth or another in a higher place, and do it so that everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back for the constriction.
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	it is necessary that you wrap it up in a cloth, as much as it comes out.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then cut at the joint of the foot or toe, and do it in the other hand, and have two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large or constricted at birth, or it has a sharp and pointed cranium.
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	it is necessary that you insert the spatula between your shoulders and shape the head and extract the sharp point.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you crush it with an instrument called "almidach", of which the shape comes with the instruments or chisel that follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and do the same in case the child has a large head naturally.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then pull out the bones with forceps.
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the jawbone springs forward and is stuck in the throat, it should be split apart until the mouth opens.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces so that you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if there is an inflammation in the abdomen or under the ribs, it is necessary to lance it as much as the mouth allows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the delivery is easy, and the approach to the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is constricted in the abdomen or chest, then it is necessary to pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and tear open the abdomen or chest, until the mouth allows it.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other limbs are broken and the jaw remains.
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then have the attendant put their hand into the womb and pull out the baby up to its mouth.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	and then insert one or two cloths, and pull it out.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the womb is constricted because of a hot inflammation that has come, then it does not need to be worked on.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	but it is necessary to apply cool and greasy things.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the ointment should be applied in the form of a poultice, soft and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it equal, then apply what we have said for a living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if they cannot move, then pull them out by parts, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if there are hot inflamations that come to the womb, then apply what we have said for them.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if there is bleeding from the delivery, then it should be applied in a constricting liquid, and other remedies should be given to her.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I have seen a woman whose womb contained a stillborn child, and she became pregnant again with another on top of it, and the second fetus killed the first one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she came to have an inflammation in her mouth, and it swelled so much that it burst open, and she began to suffer greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I looked at her for a long time, and I couldn't close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong constricting ointment to it, and out came a bone, and after a few days, another one appeared.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed greatly, because the womb had no bones in it.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a stillborn child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I cleaned the wound and pulled out more bones, until the woman was in a better state.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I took care of the woman for a long time like this, and at last she had a small piece of flesh left from the wound.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I don't recall this story except for the fact that, when a master finds an unusual thing, he knows how to help with it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the womb to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the shape of the pressor, with which we read books, and two handles for the two legs of the stool.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns are more subtle than the constriction, and they are made of ebony or boxwood.
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the handle is two fingers wide, and the edge of the wood is one finger thick, and a half-palm long.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and on the two handles there are two little clamps of the same wood, which are tightened in one and the other, half a palm long or a bit more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two clamps are inserted into the mouth of the pressor to open it when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, with its shape more subtle and lighter, is made of wood from ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of forceps.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it has two handles with two clamps, just like you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see opening the womb with all the instrument, it makes the woman sit on a bed, her feet raised and her legs wide open.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then insert the two clamps together into the womb, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with the entire instrument, just like you have done with forceps equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the womb, until the attendant makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all perfected, and their shapes are multiplied; and when the masters have perfected them, it makes the work more rapid, and more elevated among men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	It is not a wonder if you have not perfected the instrument, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you order the sick woman to retain her breath and then make her cough with condit (a type of powder or medicine), and have her restrain her hands at the mouth and neck.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she spits it out, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	And if she doesn't, then take a pot and make a hole or cover in it, and put herbs that can open the womb's mouth, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, cassis lignea, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or placed in hot water on the fire. Then take one end of the cloth or the hole from the pot and put it into the womb, and the other end should go into the mouth of the womb.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it steep until the vapors come inside the womb, then make her cough, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The afterbirth comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if the afterbirth remains after this treatment and does not come out, then order the attendant to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in mullein sap, and then insert it into the womb.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and it will take out the afterbirth; and when she has found it, then take hold of it and stretch it little by little straight out, so that the womb does not constrict during the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but you should move it gently to the right and to the left, and then pull it out; when it comes out, it will fall apart.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the womb is too constricted, we have said the treatment to cough and for fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she does not come out of all that we have said, then be careful not to pull too hard.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is in the mouth of the womb, you tie to the vulva of the woman, and then lubricate her with ointment of tetrapharmacum.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	then it will come out and go away, but however, when she bears it, a bad smell comes from the stomach and head, and harms the sick woman.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is necessary therefore to perform fumigations that are suitable for this case: none of the ancients have proven the fumigation of parsley and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at retention of the flowers and afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it looks like a cord, and one puts the thin head in the nature, and the handles are placed wide open over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be above the coals, and let it steep until it is consumed, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but rather it is closed with a very fine sponge.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	It is necessary therefore for the attendant to pierce that sponge with her finger at its tip, and not to pierce it with a pointed spatula, and to secure the ligature so that it does not come into contact.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply the ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will close again, then put in a plug of cloth or linen, and let it stay for a while, and be removed when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And if this obstruction comes suddenly from a wound or an inflammation, it is necessary to cut it out suddenly, and to treat it as we have said for the cord of linen.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from underneath the fundament are narrow and grow in length like those that come from beside the fundament outward, or in the space between the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if it has a fistula or several, and when that narrow one is old, it works out, and a moistened white or subtle pus comes out.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are closed; and they are known by the fact that there is or excretion or purulence when the sick person makes an evacuation, and by chance a fly jumps into it.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis, and reach as far as the joint of the vulva, and as high as the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows a fistula that has healed at the fundament, and not a healing one.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you insert your index finger or fundament, and insert a thin needle of iron or silver into the fistula when there is no tortuousness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuousness, then I insert a thin strip of cloth or a horsehair until you feel the strip or the hair at your tip.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there comes out from the hole excretion, purulence, or a fly, as we have said.
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	understand that it does not pierce; hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is healed up to the bladder or the channel of urine, it lets out urine, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just to the join of the hip, then the tendon comes forth just to its place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the cause of pain around it, then it means he will go lower, and there is no need for medicine or a poultice.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these Persian fistulas, there is no strong cure except travail, and vanity of foolish doctors who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In the one that is not Persian and not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lifts his legs up to his hips, and has his hips inclined towards his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put an iron needle, or a bronze one if there is twisting, as far as you know where the tendon comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then it suits that you put your second and first fingers into it.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then sense at once that the tendon has been pierced; and be discovered where you feel between your first finger and the flesh or the bone, then know it is Persian.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not hurt to pull on it, then one cannot cure it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One always says that one can very well heal some, but this is a rare thing.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that one gives it, is to cauterize a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and put it all hot in the fistula, until it reaches the fundament; and do this 2 or 3 times, as long as you know that the charred pieces are scorched, which are similar to an owl's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then heal it with moistened linen tents in butter, until the scabbed pieces fall out, and then heal it with ointment that unscabs and cures.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, it's good. If not, then it cannot be healed in any other way.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tendon is in between, and does not reach just to the bone that is at the fundament, and there is between your second finger and the tendon a thick layer of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula on what touches the cover of the bone;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cauterize from the beginning of the fistula, and put it right away before the tendon, and then apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the end of the tendon.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the tendon will be delivered and will heal; then remove those scabbed pieces that resemble an owl's feather, and there will remain nothing.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood runs out, and flows between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For cauterization with fire combines two things together: that is to say, the scorching of these joined limbs, and the burning of blood, and the drying out of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the cure of moistened tents in butter or in broth shall be boiled, until the place begins to bubble, and then it shall be poured over the burned limbs.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then cure the wound with anointed salves in great quantities of rough wood, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes right to the bottom of the foundation and is far from the body, then thrust your thumb into it or the bottom, and investigate it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the abscess and it is between two things that are the cloth or the skin or the flesh, where it is almost about to burst, then there should not be any doubt nor hope, by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you lance it right to the bottom, or if it seems to be suppurating, then you put tents and dress it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, lest you cut the tent that holds the foundation, and it will bring the purulence in a sense against your will.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then dress it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps then it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it afterwards since it is opened near the foundation, either by tent or by another instrument appointed for this purpose.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse thoroughly that foul flesh that is in the wound, as long as you can see it.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then strive to restore the wound and to close the abscess in the part far from the foundation: if it is an easier thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And never are abscesses formed in this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the abscess, and it is on the side of the foundation near the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if take a perforated tent at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and you insert one twisted thread into two, and push the tent onto all the thread in the abscess as far as the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced within the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that perforated one, just as you insert your thumb or finger.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw out the top of the thread, and tie together the two ends, and bind one to the other, and leave it for one or two days.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and you should restrain it no more, until the thread cuts through those strings that are between them, and they discharge.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then dress the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the abscess does not rupture, then make it rupture in all the ways you can think of, as long as it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a hole in the abscess that is too deep and then dress it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spur-gourd from which one makes the abscess-sponge is very sharp at both ends and has a hollow inside.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand, it is not sharp, so that one does not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the membranes.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Membranes are in two ways: or they are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they bleed freely with the blood.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and sometimes there is one or more, and are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those which are outside have little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and they bleed or there is a small amount of yellowish water or a small amount of blood, and they have the color of raw flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those that are inside the foundation, is that you command the patient to strain themselves so as to empty the chamber, and let the foundations come out, and they will see the strings.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it with pincers or by your fingernail, then cut it at its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the membranes cannot be held by their moisture, then take them on a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle over some hot powders that serve in place of cauterization.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you can cauterize them as is said in the book of cauterization, and then dress with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then cleanse the patient with a sharp and biting purgative enema to clean what is in the foundation, so that it can come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when patients are aware of their condition and the strings are visible from the foundation, then it is a light treatment.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them by your fingernail or with pincers, and cut them, then treat as we have said, until they are healed, and the patient will dread incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is fitting that you sew the wound in this manner: take one twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, then draw out the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and let it be of the right width; and bind the thread tightly, then tie the thread, draw out the needle, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one for correcting any excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put a moist cloth soaked in rose oil or cerot on the foundation, and have the patient rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it to bleed, and when they are stopped bleeding, then dress with ointment and other treatments until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the discharge of the abscess or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a discharge of abscess in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is fitting that you scrape off with the tip of a spur-gourd or your fingernail the outer layer which does not allow it to drain.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then dress it until it is closed, as is fitting.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot close, then scrape again more forcefully than before, until it heals completely and is scraped clean.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	from the abscess.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A furuncle is a small, false appearance on the skin, and it goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes when it finds a cold spot, and feels just like a dead furuncle, it spreads throughout the body, and more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread from a goose quill or a strong turkey feather, and put the thread on the furuncle, until the circles of redness surround it completely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand with all the thread until you cut around the entire furuncle, and put it deep, and extract the furuncle from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, then do as with a thread of silver or iron in this form, and be thin underneath and drawn above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers, and press it. And if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as is said in the book of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of an enema.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make an enema of silver or gold, or melted silver, and sometimes they make these little and big instruments, according to the manner in which they are introduced.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those that are introduced in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small ones.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large enema is above wide or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an aperture or the belly is tied, as you see, and the string is pierced inside; and it has two holes on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly or a bag is used to put medicines into a bladder of an animal or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and has between each hole one space, then insert into these holes a strong thread of twisted thread in ten or eleven turns, and tie the belly as one ties a kid.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then tie it with an instrument in front of a strong thread, and cleanse; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or a similar thing, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then have the patient squeeze out all their contents with both hands together, until they are completely empty, then extract the enema and raise the patient's legs to the table.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then let it flow as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps for a whole night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cleanse with an enema for the disease of bowel obstruction, and the medicine rushes out quickly, then repeat it until they are healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the foundation or growth, then the enema should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the delicate enema that the skin should be tied with.
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the section on the treatment of wounds that we would now say the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse in accordance with how they are made, and in accordance with the place or location where the wound is made, and by what means they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by falling on a stone, and the stroke of a sword or knife, or a lance or club or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made in accordance with the place of the body, such as a wound that bleeds on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head, which are simple, because the memory will come to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it was caused by falling on a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the formation of a hot apostème: if it happens at once to heal with cephalic liquid itself if it comes out pus from the wound, and the healing is on the contrary side of the damaged part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and have the patient replenish themselves with wine and large amounts of meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it doesn't heal, then reduce the amount of food and have them not drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place on the wound cotton soaked in rose oil or simply in wine stiptic.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot apostème, then place on the wound the powder I will speak of later, when it's fresh with all its blood and not altered by air or moisture.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has altered it, then apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	and if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips of the wound cannot be closed by themselves, then close them with sutures, just as I will say for belly wounds, with stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	and if the wound is exposed to the bone and raw, and only held together by a little flesh, then scrape it away; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard meat in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the patient to eat large amounts of meat, such as roasted chestnuts and bread, as well as poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a purulent skin infection that does not reach to the bone, scrape out all of it and clean, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound that cannot be stopped with a cauterizer, and it won't stop bleeding with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that doesn't help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; and it is that you put in this powder which heals even when the air has altered it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making the powder is: take equal parts of frankincense, dragon's blood, and quicksilver, and grind them finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries well and joins together all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then tie it tightly, and leave it without untying, if it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes you do this with quicksilver alone, when you don't have frankincense or dragon's blood, but the air has already altered the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the air has already changed the wound, even to an ulcer, then don't put this powder in it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made from barley flour cooked in water and honey, until it discharges pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break in the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there should be no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment alone and put nothing restraining, because it hurts the nerves and makes them contract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but apply warm medicine to it, such as dissolved quicksilver in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber juice also dissolved in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other powdered minerals in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and tie with bandages, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and open and filled with pus, then lance them or lower part of it.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then uncover it, tie off the ends, and cauterize as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the esophagus of the throat is cut or the gullet, and the conduit is kept, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	then sew up the gullet above the chin of the throat, and do not touch the throat but place it back in its natural position.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it properly, and leave it for some days, then treat it with purging ointments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then scrape it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then extract them all if you can, and what you cannot take out, let it stay until the wound becomes purulent.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and have the issue drained and bound tightly.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and a fistula, then treat it in the manner that I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a cut from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, then look to see if there is windiness coming out of the wound that makes the patient faint: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put powder on it at first hour nor tie it up for the bleeding that does not stop in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and revive to the heart, and kill the patient. (Note: This seems to be a statement of a grim outcome, rather than an actual medical instruction)
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, then put clean cotton in the wound to suck out moisture and blood.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep over the wound for 3 days, or 4 days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if it doesn't come with a spasm, nor a bad trembling of the heart and no sign of fainting.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with stitches and other treatments, until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and becomes infected, then know that there is an abscess; and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife and it is simple, or worse on the back, then treat as those in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, by stitching; and if it is small, with powder; and if it has made an impression in the bone and has cut off pieces, then scrape out the wound, and extract the pieces if they are loosened.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loosened, then let the wound become purulent, so that it will draw out the pieces.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members, the judgments are as we have said earlier.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of intestinal rupture.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the intestines is great, middle-sized and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Sometimes from a large wound the intestines or the membranes of the intestines burst forth, through which there is an entrance.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes is worse than a small wound than a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for this reason one should not sew the intestines in with pins if they are not sewn hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, and will not be pinned back in.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason it is better to suture the smaller wound, because one must sew the intestine back into place rather than others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitches for other wounds of the body and the two other proper stitches are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and in any case they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine sticks out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if there is nothing to be stitched, it is done by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	wet a sponge or a soft cloth with lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or boil it in warm water with cinnamon and spice.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and soak the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and once you have done this, restrain it and note that it has only swollen in order to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, then moisten the intestine with warm or hot water and let it be cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by that the entrance of the gut is freed from some things.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small pouch with the wound and use the instrument with which one probes hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to cut it.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut it unless there is great necessity for it.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut inside in the curve and then back out, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines spring out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its proper place according to its natural form.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you can't, because this is a must.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part under the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is advisable that you make the patient lie on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part under the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then place the head and chest higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and similarly if the wound of the belly is in one of the two parts,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then incline yourself so that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is advisable to remember what I say about great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, apply the ointment that suits you.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take in your hands one gentle surgeon who will touch the whole wound with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips of the wound.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common manner of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and then take a needle or needles, according to the size of the wound's width,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound a space of about two fingers in length, and put a needle there where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce through both ends of the skin with the two eyes of the syringe (or possibly "sphac", which might be a type of needle).
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is on the inside of the skin, so that you make it pierce through from that side.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two ends of the syringe (or possibly "sphac"), in three turns.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then take a doubled thread and wind it around the needle from both sides.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then bring together the two ends of the wound in a good way,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave another space of about two fingers in length, and put another needle there;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread so that you have done it in the same way as the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this until you need more needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the smaller and larger needles be between fine and coarse.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the very fine needles pierce the flesh too easily, and the ones that are too coarse cannot go in well at all.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is advisable for them to be moderate.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not advisable to push the needles too far out of the flesh and the skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not pierce and open up the wound in front of the stitch.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then remove the needles' points so that they will not prick the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put threads or cloths on the needle's points to hold them firmly,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of stitching with needles is more advisable in small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because only one needle or two are needed.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common.
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you bring together the two ends of the skin and the two ends of the thread, both together, on one needle where there is a strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these ends together in three turns,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then roll the needle to the part where you started it, in the manner that one sews clothing.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch the size of a small two fingers.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is called the "homme's" (man's) stitch.
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I stitched a wound that a man had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was wounded by a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's length in width,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were well exposed for two palms' length.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly itself.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestines then, after it had been exposed for 24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed in just 15 days, and he was cured, and he was healthy again.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not heal him with ointment, because I was in a place where there wasn't any to be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put old linen cloth over the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and insert it from the outside part to the inside part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the skin straight through, then take the end of the thread or sewing needle and push it through where you inserted the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from the inside to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the meaning of this stitch is that you sew just like a tailor makes seams in leather.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave the thread on one side and pick it up from the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galien calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is to sew the two parts together naturally, just like others do, who bring them together in one piece.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the thread to the other end, in this same way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	put a needle or the eye of the thread close by, and make it pierce only that place.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle around and make it pierce from the outside part to the inside part.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	leaving the two ends of the thread.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and then the other from the outside part to the inside part, in two other eyes of thread that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien says these words, and many people testify to them.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each one.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must insert one needle from one side and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is on the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the most difficult stitch of all other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as that of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood still in it, just as the heat has changed,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then it must be closed again, covering the intestines and the cut, then apply powder to the inflamed flesh.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the heat has changed it, then apply any salve that is available until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew the thread, and sew together the needle and the thread.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound just like the others, until it is healthy again.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then apply old cotton as soon as possible, so that the wound begins to heal.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and remove it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you don't need any other medicine in most cases, where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound is causing commotion among the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	it is advisable that you soak linen lightly in hot temperate oil or in rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the joints and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or torment in the bowels, and often vomits,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then cleanse him with black vinegar enemas, and similarly if the torment comes up to the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "young" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the tenderness of their walls and the subtlety of the entire body and its approach to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts from the wound, then close it again as the intestines are closed, while it is still fresh.
