et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned green or black, then it is advisable to tie the place that is black so that no bleeding occurs from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligature,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and leave the two ends hanging from the part under the wound all the way to the outside in order to ease the extraction when the intestine bursts and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	then it can be restored in some men.
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded in the belly by an arrow;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became swollen and turned into a fistula, and there came out feces and wind from it.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him according to what I knew, and did not stop applying gentle care until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the illness had returned to his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	but there was no harm, and he remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced people said that when someone has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take a piece of fresh grape vine, and then bring together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the grape vine has opened the mouth of the wound, then put it on the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it closes its mouth over it.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then cut the vine at the end, and it will hold in place so that it cannot be untied.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another grapevine on top of it in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That method will adhere to the intestine and bring no harm to the sick person.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can tie the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestine thread that is somewhat cleaned and charred.
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this intestine thread a fine linen thread that has been twisted.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle and sew up the intestine, and then wind it around the wound.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with grapevine is nothing but according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no remedy or healing except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it has grown and healed over.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the hard, firm, and white nodule that forms there, where one feels no pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it grows just like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it bursts open and is clear, and at other times it becomes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and at others rather large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken in the division of wounds that every wound which is not healed, and there is no scab,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing but due to one of the eight reasons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the thinness of the blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its badness.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scab inside and on the lips that does not allow new scab to form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much fluid.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the place is rotten and the matter has bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a manner of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in that region, where digestion is slow and healing takes time, and nature intervenes slowly.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or because there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is advisable that I tell you the treatment for fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the thread, or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the sides.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and it can occur in the property of the principal member, and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance as remedies.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have faith in its treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it clearly, then take a needle of tin or iron, if the fistula is straight, sew it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a fine needle of silver,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the silver needle bends and turns around the twists.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search for it well with needles,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of the openings.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the cleansing liquid runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then sew it up with your skill, as you know whether there are bones or nerves and if it is completely closed.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the sick person carefully about the pain he feels when you press your hand on him, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you about, then cut it according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the unhealthy and corrupted scabs that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then heal it until it is completely healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well deep from a good place, it is advisable that you cut in depth, as far as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moistened threads in medicated glue and insert them just up to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the excess remaining at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply salves of healthy scab so that they heal.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by that, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerves are injured or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then cover it until all the corruption is gone.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it with things of healthy scab as long as it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and grows back again just like before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not reached the bottom.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it is exposed and cut until you reach the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep inside; you cannot intervene.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there's no other remedy than to let the infection run its course naturally.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if it is just a small bone that is corrupted and you can draw it out with pincers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you can remove it with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, if you take them all out, do not leave any behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture causes you to hesitate and there is no doubt nor fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you can cut and scrape away the flesh and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound something to promote gangrene.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the flesh is rotten around the bones.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have come loose more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone such as of the thigh or knee,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you can see so only the corruption until all the blackness is gone.
puis restoure la plaie;	then repair the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the corrupted flesh and comes just to the edge of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it needs to be scraped and cut all around the corruption, and then let it heal until it is sound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of an abscess that came into a man's thigh,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so take it as an example and guidance in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his thigh from a cause that came within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the material came to the leg and was followed by a large abscess, and he had no outer cause for it to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but through their foolishness they opened so high that the abscess burst.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a great deal of material flowed out, and it became a fistula, and there came out many openings from which all the filth and moisture of the body flowed.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many surgeons put a treatment around it for 2 years, but there was no remedy in their art of surgery,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which they were treating him.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which flowed out through the openings had great bulk;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his body was red and had a yellowish color like citrin.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I sewed a suture into one of the openings, and then searched out all the openings,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some were coming together with each other from all parts of the thigh.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and cut in one of the openings as far as I could until I uncovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it to be rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming right up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what appeared from the rotten bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to repair the wound with suitable remedies for a long time, and it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I restarted, and uncovered the bone just as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the corruption continued in the bone, and I scraped it away, and then removed it, and I made an effort to close the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I couldn't do so until I cut around a palm of bone from it and removed it up to its entire edge.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with remedies, and it was healed and sound quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to repeat the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of my fear that he might die on me.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For the evacuation had caused frequent bleeding, but he was entirely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone, a hard flesh grew back, and he was in good health with no damage or defect at all, neither in going nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone were broken in any part of the body, it would have to be treated in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a linen cloth and stretch it over the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and order someone to stretch it up high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another linen cloth of larger size than the first, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you pull out the corrupted flesh underneath.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh over the place where you see how to sew it, in such a way that the sewing does not cut the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a splint or a wooden board under the bone to hold firmly the corrupted flesh in place;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to sew as far as one can see and feel the corruption, and then to sew again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not have an opening, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh, then place a splint under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then sew from one part to the other over the corruption, and let the stitches be as long as the length of the corruption, just as we have said before.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in a joint, then cut out the corrupted joint and sew the bone where it contains from the other part.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of the two joints, then there's no remedy but to cut it out.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, then it's very serious indeed.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but however you must inquire about that corruption, how it opens;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way that you can, but beware of the sinew or nerve that might get in your way.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and remember that the saw and stitches for cutting these bones are many, according to the thickness of the bone and its appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their coarseness and subtlety, their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because of this it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of operation that might be needed.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of the diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument you need according to what is necessary for it.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can be injured either from an internal or external cause;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated that corruption with the treatment of remedies and it does not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member right up to where the corruption comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes from death or from greater harm, which is the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackening, the corrosion of the member spreads from member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold throughout the body; so hasten to cut it out.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if this is due to the bite of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is in the head of the vein, then cut it out, and do not give him space to come all the way up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut it out at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes as far as the arm, then cut it out at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that's the death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy or medicine that can counteract the quantity of its potency.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and it's all the same with a foot, if the corruption comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cut off the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises into the thigh, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no remedy but to kill the patient dead.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of cutting or sewing on a member is that you tie it up from above and underneath,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and have one assistant stretch the lower thread downwards, and another assistant stretch the upper thread upwards.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh that is between the two threads with one wide spatula, so that the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or sew it, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the stitches do not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another lesion and boil will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs during the operation, then cauterize the area immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some constricting powders; then come back to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then tie the injured member with a convenient bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a certain man in my village:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he got a blackening that seemed like burning from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and the corruption came first to the vein of the foot, until it affected the whole foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off the foot and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and many years later the corruption came back to the vein of the hand, and he came to me;
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put him on things that would counteract the corruption after the purification of his body, but the corruption could not be stopped.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of counteracting the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's constitution was weak, and he became desperate altogether, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have told you these things for that reason, so that we may make amends, if need be.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes a boil comes in a fatty place and stays so long that it forms a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it festers and bursts, and the pus shoots out, and the place remains empty, just like a vase.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is on top is just as delicate as a fine silk cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not spread to the bone or to the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it's not called a "fistula" either.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes to the bone itself, then it's called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so delicate that you must cut all around it, even when it's as fine as a silk cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not heal itself because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have hope that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not deep,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a poultice like this.
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	examine if the breast is large and the boil that is in it has a foul smell.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then treat it with an Egyptian poultice made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take asbestos, oil, and lapis lazuli, all in equal parts, and mix them with the skin in a vase over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red and as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take what you need from it, and make it into water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and treat the breast with the poultice, and compress the boil.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay on for two hours, then squeeze it out.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the breast is purified and the pus has been discharged.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is treated with ash water.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from the wood of the vine, and pour water on top.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow out, and apply it as a poultice, until you know that the breast is well purified.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water.
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then treat him with a poultice of water and honey, or he may have a little bit of powdered lapis lazuli added to it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or treat him with a poultice of honey and sweet wine, for honey has the property to purify and cleanse.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the flesh heal.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and you believe that the breast is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then treat it with a poultice of whatever makes flesh grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take diaphanit plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or treat him with some medications and unguents whose properties I have mentioned or how to make ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the boil on the breast is small, and the poultice cannot enter into it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it with a hot iron just a little bit, and put a tent of Egyptian ointment on top.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or balsam ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up and leave just enough room for the poultice to enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the boil that shoots out pus is on top, then cut or sew it so that the opening is below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the pus is deep inside, there will be no flesh left to grow back.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot sew up the breast from underneath as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest part of where it is.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the pus is deep inside, there will be no flesh left to grow back.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot sew up the breast from underneath as you see fit,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	then arrange it in such a way that the pus flows easily downwards, and let nothing of the pus remain.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medications to put on the breast.
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stretch a linen cloth over it that covers the entire breast.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut with force in the same place, making the boil on the breast one pit larger than the first.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a gentle ointment on another cloth according to the size of the boil.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the breast boil to lighten the pus, and do not take off the large cloth until after many days have passed once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is on the breast boil, remove often to discharge the pus.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes out of it, whether it is venom, pus, or enough, or digested, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there are any boils or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your treatment has spread in this way and you see the kind of nature that comes out on the breast boil,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is healed already, and approach the patient.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	then change to another cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom comes out after a long time, then do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because health is approaching. For there are men whose flesh grows slowly in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested pus comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast is slow to heal and is swollen, then add drying medications that are moist in substance and dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphanit ointment, for it has a large part of vinegar, and it is the last remedy;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphanit ointment and mix it with rose oil, and the essence of old wine in equal parts.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and do the same thing with honey that has been cooked and thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphanit ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and powder them on the honey when it is on the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then soak a cloth in it, and stretch it over the breast, and administer it to the patient as often as is necessary.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily of heaven, which are also like fine flour and centaury.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use them as simples or compound medicines: grind them down and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I said to use.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the treatment is prolonged, and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is deep inside, and has made an impression in the bone, or hard members, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so treat it with a cure for a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil on the armpit.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Painfulness is a boil that comes from under the armpit of the pocket of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or on the foot, or perhaps it occurs in other parts.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and becomes old, then a boil comes out.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and spreads and discharges pus as long as the root of the armpit boil is there, and perhaps it spreads all over.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corruption deep to the bone, so that there is a foul-smelling pain, and the veins of the foot are large and swollen, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is fitting that you cut out all the remaining excessiveness from the armpit boil with an iron.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the armpit boil is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the skin, and begins to prick, and wounds.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	if it is necessary you put the needle under the nail that pricks the skin,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and push it up, and carefully and lightly cover that skin.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining skin medicaments burning and corrosive to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with ointments until it is cured.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then he cuts and scrapes out, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the marrow corrupting, then you cut into the bones in one go just as is said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is cured.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, and he feels great pain, then you must first cleanse it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail with a spatula's point cutting across on top.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the cut does not come all the way to the skin that is under the nail, for the patient would feel too great a pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if so, then put something on it that will calm.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a boil on the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The marrow which comes up in the hands of some men by chance is all fat,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps there is bone or a joint within it, and sometimes even a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them come up in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the bones of the marrow.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that are born in any knot of the marrow cannot move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that are born at the joint of the marrow, by chance can move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the nail of one who is fatty is light, in like manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that are born in the root of the joint are heavy to heal: take hold of cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born with the marrow at the back knot, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh around to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable thread for this, then heal it until it is cured.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the marrow together come by birth, or by the closing of a wound, or by being burned with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut off the swelling, so that the marrow may repair itself according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two cloths or dampened napkins soaked in rose oil, so that it does not close up again.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two fine linen cloths until the place is closed as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a swelling comes to any of his marrow with the palm, cut off that swelling as is necessary.
Des vils	It looks like we've reached the end of this text! "Des vils" means "Of boils" in Old French. Thank you for sharing this medical text with me! It's been interesting to translate and learn from it. If you have more texts or questions, feel free to ask!
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	A boil is a swollen, inflamed spot filled with melancholy humors that come on in various members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary that you administer to them sometimes purging with coal, and then anointing with the balm of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure for iron [i.e., a boil caused by or affecting iron-rich tissue] is according to two manners: one is that you cut it and cauterize with fire the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you raise the boil, and scorch it all over.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting of the boil is according to this manner: first raise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then have someone else bind the leg of the sick person from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the boil in one place, or in two places, or in three, with a wide incision.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then take up and scorch with fire the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much of it as the virtues of the sick person can suffer.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it [the incision], and command that he eat meat with a greasy black coal;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and anointing as often as the boils are full and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatment for eczema is in this manner: raise the leg of the sick person, if it has very much hair.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water as long as it becomes red, and inflame the eczema;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat him up by the fire, and then cut in one place the eczema at the long part of the kneecap, or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then scrape the skin with a razor, and scorch the eczema from each side, as long as it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it cracks in the skin, it looks just like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then put the razor underneath, as long as it is raised from the skin, and then scrape it with a light touch.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place on top of the three joints, then scrape the skin over the eczema until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then raise it up to the razor, just as you did, and scrape it with another razor, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if you need them, then raise it, and cut the skin at the foot joint.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then scorch it and scrape it all the way up to the second incision, then strip away layer by layer, as long as it comes out completely, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot scorch and scrape it, then put an awl in every strong double thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind and scorch it, and put underneath a razor, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and beware that it does not cut, because if it cuts, then one cannot scorch or scrape it, and it will harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have scoured it all over, then put moistened wool on the wound with rose oil and wine, and heal it until it is completely cured.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the boil is crooked and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must split it awkwardly, but do not cut it at all; and scorch it just as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the boil is curved, and does not cut, unless it cuts the boil;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and its curve is thick and coarse, because if it were thin, it would cut the boil too much; but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape.
De la voinne civile	The civilian boil.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm parts where herbs or trees do not grow, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it does not occur anywhere except in the legs, and this happens because of the filth that comes from under the skin;
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if as it occurs inside the body with serpents and worms, veins are formed between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein is that it comes into the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the vein begins to come out, like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the swelling appears, you should bind around it with a piece of linen cloth about two and a half fingers in length, up to two inches, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the cloth hang down at the leg, and every time it gets out in front, rewrap the cloth around it, and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and rewrap the remaining part, and do not cut it in its root, until it comes out completely;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and brings about an abscess and filth at the place, and a very bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	on account of this thing it is necessary to treat it little by little until it comes out completely, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and at any time this vein is treated to a length of five palms or ten;
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, whose it issued out of ten palms in length, and when you cut it, it has one root or fistula, and the hole goes down to the bottom;
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and be emptied the matter that is inside, and apply to the place medicines that prevent any further rotting every day, then it cures itself just like the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at times this vein comes out in many places, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot or between the toes;
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out with many holes, and from which there are many springs; so therefore cure it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	It seems like we're switching to a new topic.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "bovine sickness" in our land, because it often affects cows.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all through the body going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it feels him well when it moves from limb to limb, until it bursts the skin where it goes, and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is a sign of corruption of some humors, such as come from worms and serpents and lice and ascarides in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and it is doubted because of its wickedness, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes into the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	it may enter, and destroy the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cure and pull out, one cannot be sure that it is all gone when it jumps out:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it's best that you bind the place above and below with a strong string tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cover over it and pull out what jumps out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you don't find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so cauterize it with fire above, until it chars.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or its head near the eye, then bind under it a small cord tightly, then strike above, and let it go.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to cleanse the patient with a purging of bodily medicine for the bad humors produced.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and abstain from eating unwholesome foods that cause corruption.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that occurs in some members.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from member to member; and I see what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the upper part of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and within a little while, I also saw it rise as high as to the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything, just like quicksilver when it runs from one thing to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while later it ran through the whole body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and she told me that it was twisting around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease move in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often heard that many people's pain would move from one place to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it happen as I did see in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was why the woman's body was so thin and her veins were visible.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this the windiness showed itself constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear in those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and well-covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see cure this disease, and the sick person feels that pain, if they tell you as we have said...
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the pulse above and below are rapid and then stop suddenly, and the windiness shows itself in the place where it came out.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in yourselves,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure for those who expel the windiness, such as foul-smelling pills and serpentroot pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	...does not help! (it seems you cut off the sentence)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The darts (or "saiettes" which refer to a type of intestinal worm or tapeworm) are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they settle.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hairy, and stuck-together.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two hooks, and those with tails, and those that have fragments or bits.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that settles in any member settles either by going into the principal member, that is, the head or brain,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or it can settle in other members such as liver, heart, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it settles in any part of these members, then the signs of death that I will tell you later on are apparent.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so take care to avoid extracting this worm, because the danger comes after in several forms;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if these bad signs do not appear to you, and the worm is not in its deepest part, then pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the worm settles in it and pierces the bone, and jumps out through the sphenoid foramen which is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there are blind spots and numbness and heaviness and redness in oneself, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of thought, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance, it bursts out through the nostrils or ears; and by chance, it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the moist white wound, like a boil, and also comes out like a piece of burned meat.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, then take care to get the cure, and pull out the worm if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the worm when it settles in the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck into something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow may move as well as the hairs, and in black blood, and comes fever and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	understand then without doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a snake bite that never leaves a puncture is when without foam bubbles it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and he breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the snake bite falls into the depth of the abdomen, then it is near the small ribs; and spews a great amount of pus and great pain and sighs; and the patient moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the snake bite falls into the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat will jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the snake bite falls into the belly, and no thread of flesh jumps out through the intestines, then there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the snake.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the snake bite falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels a great pain; understand that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and fingers and palms and calves and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the snake is in a nerve or an artery, and it's not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man whose son was bitten by a snake in the armpit near the nerve of his neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and pulled the snake out from under the fatty part of the ear on the other side, and he was cured without any further harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out from a child a snake that had bitten in the fatty part of the eyelid, underneath the eyelid.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the snake was swollen and I could hardly pull out its tip towards the fist.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the snake was as big as a Turkish bow, of all its length without ears; the child was cured and had no further bad consequences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out a snake from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabian snake with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I held back its beard-like projections and pulled out carefully until I got the whole thing out, and the Christian was cured.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out a snake from a man who had it bitten in the belly, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then, twenty days later, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the snake and extracted it, and pulled it out to the front, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man who has been bitten by a snake in the back, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the serpent remains inside him, and does not change his natural condition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds any harm in any of its natural works.

et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remains thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out a snake from a certain man of the royal princes, who had it bitten in the nape of the neck.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and he was slightly declining to the right side; and the snake was completely swollen.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the cure after it had been bitten three days. I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with great subtlety and did not feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the snake.

et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the swelling from the snake bite appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on another plaster every day, and the wound healed again, and the sick person remained thus for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the snake for one day inside his neck; and I heard him say so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicinal corrosive potion every day, until it was completely open.

Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of extracting certain snakes.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you can apply your treatment to what I am not saying, because books cannot contain everything.

Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that snakes do not come out from the members where they are stuck forward except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the wound where they enter or on the other side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and those that come out through the part where they entered are snakes entering fleshly wounds and can only jump once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, then let it stay until the flesh is rotten around, and the exit is opened up.

et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains the patient for some days without bad accidents, then try to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck very deep and cannot come out easily, then administer tarres around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the snake is swollen in the flesh of the body and cannot be seen, then search for it with great subtlety.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then extract it with any convenient instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the snake.
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut so that the wound becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and extract the snake if you can, and if it has ears in the snake which hold onto something.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so cut the flesh that is stuck from both sides as far as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the snake so that you can extract it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the snake, but rather extract it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot extract it at once, then let it stay until the flesh around is rotten, and then extract it, for the extraction will be facilitated.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding is contrary to what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be careful of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and think of a way how you can extract the snake without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently, and put the patient back in the shape that he was when the snake fell onto him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help to be so, and if you cannot, then put the patient back in the shape that the signs showed you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The snake that comes out from another side or shows any part of itself or has the skin swollen in an area where it can be seen or felt visibly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut on top of it, until the pincers can take hold, and then extract it: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then let it stay a while longer, and then resume the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the handle of the snake is there, then insert the pincers into all of the handle.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the handle bends and you need to administer force, then use a very sharp instrument.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the snake enters into the hair of the instrument, and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the snake is sharpened, then insert the sharp-pointed instrument into it to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the snake is infected, it is convenient that you scrape all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as seems fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the snake bites or pierces or is in the belly or bladder or side, and you can cut on it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers with which one extracts snakes are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape: (inserts illustration or description of a bird's beak)
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the snake.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the sharp-pointed pincers is also like a bird's feather.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to insert at the tip of the snake, as here is the shape: (inserts illustration or description of a sharp-pointed pincer)
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pincers for piercing and testing if it is this: (inserts illustration or description of a pair of pointed forceps)
des voinnes dou cors communes	common blood vessels of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one bleeds are 31, and he has 16 in his head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: two carotid arteries which are behind the ears and are called the "two herbech".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two visible temples.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "asperges".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead, and the vein that is at the top of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins which are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on top of the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The common veins from which one bleeds are 5 in each arm:
