l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein and it is from the left side of the chest, and common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "brachial" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the fold.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one from which one bleeds, which appears clearly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the Salvatelle vein is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the fold of the left side of the thigh.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is the saphenous vein that is at the ankle of the right side, and the vein called "Nesse" that is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears is helpful to ancient Catholics and to migraine sufferers.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the bather, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth, then bind the patient's neck with a strap to a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in their respective places dependent on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then ask your doctor to sign it, and where you feel the pulse below your elbow, if they seal it.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and push it under the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand up to all of the vein upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and scrape the skin and vein very well on both sides of the intersection, and let out blood until you see that it is finished.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind and tie it, so that it becomes healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for ancient migraines.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and headache, and usual conjunctivitis, and sharp pain in the eyes' pupils.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the bather is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient binds their neck, so that the two veins appear clearly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse below your elbow, and then seal it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the skin up over the vein above your index finger, and push the lancet under.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein upwards, and cut it, just like you have done in the other two veins, and let out blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then untie the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put a compress on top of it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it securely and leave it until it is healed. And we have already spoken of its scraping and extraction in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is worth just as much as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient face diseases, and migraines, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient binds their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is this: (inserts illustration or description of a surgical instrument)
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point of the "fosseur" on the vein, and push upwards with your hand or other object, and let out blood as you see fit.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then untie the patient's neck and tie the vein so that it is healed, and at no time let there be a faint scar or an ugly mark.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable that the scars are too sharp and the bleeding cuts across, because the bone is close and by chance the scars may break through when they become subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the corners of the eyes is helpful for eye diseases, and for conjunctivitis, and for redness, and for irritation in the eye, and for face diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient binds their neck by twisting it in some way, just like before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bleed, and the bleeding of the cut should be a bit long and a bit wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the scar is subtle and by chance breaks through, then let out blood as needed, and then bind it with cotton and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the vein on the nose is worth for acute fever, and for severe headache, and face diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraines and redness that come to the face, and especially when it is ancient.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient binds their neck, then ties their nose with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the thin long thread and insert it between the two nostrils in the space that is between them.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not appear well there, and now the blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep in there, and let out blood as needed, then bind it for a night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the thread: (inserts illustration or description of a thin, long thread)
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two jugular veins is helpful for the constriction of the throat, and for the beginning of inflammation, and for many diseases, and for epidemic, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and swelling.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient binds their neck under both jugular veins, just as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the masters are standing on the head of the patient, and the patient is sitting on one seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the vein longly a bit wide, then draw out blood temperately, or as much as needed is.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then redo the other part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and bind it around the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke, and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On the cure of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The salt of the veins above the lips helps to draw blood in the mouth, and corrupts the gums, and splits the lips, and brings down the teeth and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the salt are to make the sick person sit in front of you, and hold their chin as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the small black lines around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	so then cover one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt;
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	so cover the thicker one from each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the salt under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The salt of the veins that are under the tongue also helps after the salt of the cerebral vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the salt are that the sick person sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks under on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then salt both, but do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the throat which are commonly salted are salted in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by piercing with a full-sized, pointed myrrh twig, or with a subtle olive branch like the cuttings of the cistus (a type of evergreen), and it is called "Anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and their width and subtlety are according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the myrrh twig is very well-known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it needs to open the veins that are covered with thick, visible blood, and that contain thick and turbid blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that is the shape of the olive twig:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed, and is for salting the finer veins, where there is fine, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The salt of the cerebral vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the salter to salt carefully, and to beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he pierces the artery, and blood begins to flow out, then it needs to be staunched, just as I said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the twig should not be pierced, but rather cut in such a way that it is like Anesil (the olive twig).
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the cerebral vein does not open visibly, then you need to twist and remove it, and take another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or else you want a drop of its blood, or you salt in place of it the vein in the arm: it opens visibly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and pierce with the myrrh twig Anesil, just as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the saltation, then it is necessary that you twist the arm, until you touch the place as far as you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot with ink, and then bind the arm, and pierce the vein with the myrrh twig Anesil.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the spot swollen, for it is the artery: flee from it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see come out in the same way as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is the blood of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put on your doublet slowly, and take out your doublet if the blood is staunched, for it has happened many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	bind the arm and leave it so, and do not move it until the malady is cured; and be on guard, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched, and it flows out, and the medicine is not present, then pierce the artery if it appears, for the head of the vein retreats; and stanch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a peel of figs, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind it well up to the other joint;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	And if the blood is staunched, it's good; and if not, then apply a remedy, as we have said, with powders that stanch blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stauching is not in vain on more occasions for the small size of the wound and the weakness of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The saltation of the vein in the middle helps to treat bleeding from the head above and the belly below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the cerebral vein and the cephalic vein, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the salter to beware of the nerve that is underneath, and if he pierces too deeply, he will find the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the cure is in vain, and by chance cannot be cured.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens up many times, and since it is very subtle in some men, you need to take out the saltation with the instrument Anesil, and flee from the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, split it longways.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The saltation of the cephalic vein helps to treat bleeding from the head and is useful for them.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to salt in piercing with the olive twig flame or with the myrrh flame, because it is the most safe of all veins, because there are no nerves nor arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to find the lightest place and not hurt anything if we fail the first time, and try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and in some cases, the places swell up in some people when we fail the first time, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the saltation is according to your thought. (meaning that the success or failure of the procedure depends on the skill and judgment of the person performing it)
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about salting is that saltation is not made to be hurried, but rather for preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and in order to flee from the upcoming illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the saltation be done in one of the three veins that are outside: which is to say, the cephalic vein, the facial vein, and the basilic vein.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it should be salted in the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and it should be salted on the first day or the third day after 2 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The saltation that is administered for illnesses has no fixed time determined, but rather as soon as the need arises by day or by night, at all hours and in all circumstances.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to salt children until they are 14 years old, nor women who are pregnant except in the last month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be salted.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be salted, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that they cleanse the bowels with a light purge.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there are many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the superfluities and harmful residues towards the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should those who are too salty from meats, nor those who are drunk, as long as it lasts, nor dropsy patients be salted.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and beware of salting after a passionate colic, and vomiting, and bloating of the belly, and multiple visits to women, and hard work, staying up late, and getting tired, and all things that exhaust the virtue, either by thing of arm or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and by remedies, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter into a bath, if nothing hinders you, to subtlety the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and salt yourself from the vein of the liver around the third part, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard that day from work, and piercing, and lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be happy and joyful, and let the salter be higher than the one who is being salted, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then gently stretch out the ligature above, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell and you feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the salter's flame with the oil from a old flask, then put his hand of his left arm above that vein below the place where he wants to salt.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not dry out and be damaged by piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that are as thin as strings when being salted, and some of them are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when the flame is put on it, it retreats back and cannot open up the vein, and such are the ones.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it closes up the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for that reason it is necessary for the salter to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens up the first time, it's good; and if not, then try again after a little while in that same place or above hastily, unless the swelling is already present.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen and the sickness is worsening, let it be for one day or two days without binding the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps abscesses will come; don't go into the bath, then try again with the saltation if it pleases you.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it's not as much blood as you see, pierce in that same opening directly with all the flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and it will open up a bit hastily, so that the place is swollen; for such things happen many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, don't try again with the saltation, and put on a bit of oil there, because it lightens the body of the blood, and is moistened in that same place where the oil lies.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each saltation that you make for the veins, to stop the flow of the blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing is done with triacle and powdered water, when it is put on the place; it subtlety the blood and disperses it when it becomes too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a big abscess, which has happened many times, especially when the saltation was not made strongly enough at that time or the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hurry and put on the place a moist sponge in hot water and vinegar for a short time, and strain it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, and if a blackness or greenish color remains at the place after some days, it does not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on something made with aloes or myrrh mixed with wine of calaminth, mastich, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance have occurred in the saltation of the basilic vein: so put your hand on it then, and if you find that place soft to the compression of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So avoid putting on anything of what we have said, for it may cut the blood from the artery; but make one dry poultice to harden the place, then dress it with another dressing until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each kind of blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see that it is abundant, let it flow until it becomes subtlety; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is fat and full-bodied, and has need of letting out blood, that we make a larger wound, and have the flames wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and make it smaller and more often salted, and it should be salted by piercing in a crossed way, not in a direct way.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of salting is safe from bleeding and cutting of nerves, and is worth more than the saltation of length or breadth.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body is weakened by salting, it is necessary to give him a moist compress soaked in juice of green apples; if he is fevered, treat the blood three times or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he has a cold complexion, mix before salting a moist compress with sweet syrup or with aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he sweats during salting, after the bleeding has stopped, it is necessary that he sniff broth of meat and a subtle aromatic syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and follow the other things we have said in the chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to relieve his arm and heal it again, then it is necessary, when it is weakened by great hemorrhage, that he let the blood flow gradually, little by little, according to the quantity of his strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong veins, then he bleeds .vij. hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another place, then he must be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood inside the body which is already heated up and makes fever; then it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and to enlarge the incision so that it reaches to the parmacum.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then since you are making incisions for bleeding, and place your hand on the pulse while it bleeds, so that the more blood does not come in place of the venous humor.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the one who is bleeding is neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not seem good when you want to untie the arm, and let blood come out the second time, and the incision is closed, that you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, that he straightens the arm quickly, for it would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him leave it so that the blood flows out again the second time; or you prick to the tip of the flame, until the frozen blood comes out through the vein's opening.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on .i. pot of cold water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not bind it up again, until the inflammation has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to let out blood a second time, then bleed from the same place, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm have been bled in place of those of the head because they are composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method for bleeding is that the patient dips their hand into hot water until the pulse (foscile) is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then he should be bound moderately tight, so that the vein appears well, then let him bleed now across, not through the length or width.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the incision be wide and let him bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if the blood does not come out, then put the hand in hot water and let it cool down until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not put the hand in hot water at all, for one puts it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding from this vein is safer from all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve nearby.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The bleeding of the median cubital vein of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the arm, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the bleeding is across, and you cut from top to bottom all the way through, then it hurts nothing.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep in it, for the nerves are under the skin, denuded of flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let out enough blood, then put oil and a thread on the vein to sew it up quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding on the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do everything in the same way as I told you to do with the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The bleeding of the subclavian vein is worth for all diseases that are under the body, (i.e. internal organs).
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of urine, and disease of the bowels, and of the old joints and limbs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient dips their foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it swells.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and bind above the joint of the foot; and the vein is near the ankle, and from there to the foot there are many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	bleed it then at the largest vein or at the ankle, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it above the foot, be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and the bleeding will come out also like cutting, and the wound will be quickly healed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood does not come out, then put the foot in water again and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bleeding does not come out the first time, then try again the second time above a spot, because the place is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor fear of nerves, as we have said, and do the same with the subclavian vein of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The seat of the sciatic vein is at the knee, and its bleeding is worth for pain in the back, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient enters or bathes in warm water and strains above the knee with four threads twisted together.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not appear; and if it appears, then bleed in all the ways you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is worth more than any other vein, for the place is good, and it is very near to many people's hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then bleed any vein that appears behind the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much as to let out enough blood that you see it, and then release the tie, and put on cotton and bind it tight; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Here we go again!
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or of horn, or of glass; and bloodletting is done in two ways: either by pricking and attracting blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this bloodletting that is done without pricking is in two ways: either it is done with fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and bloodletting that is done by pricking and extraction of blood is done in fourteen places on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is on the top of the head, and the others are in the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on both sides of the neck, and the leech under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the leechs on the upper arms; and the leech above the kidneys.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the leechs in both arms; and the leechs in both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the leechs on the soles of the feet; and bloodletting does not take out blood, unless it is small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason they do not weaken anyone much, as when one takes out blood from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not suitable that it be administered, either with fire or without fire, in any illness that comes from overfilling, until the entire body has been drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illness or habit it is necessary to bloodlet, let us administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such people who, when they need to bloodlet, have a heavy head,
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who find fullness and darkness in their face, and on their head, and neck, and have a cloudiness of themselves.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people find a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen, and they are short of breath.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such people who swoon, and see through the blood vessels, and see navel strings and wounds and dead things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even more so if it is in the middle of the month, let us command them to be bloodlet after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The mucus of the nose helps with the clearing of the head... that comes to us, and it is not suitable that this be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this poultice is in place of the salve for the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not suit those who have a cold constitution or who are sick with catarrh, for it causes them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it does not suit the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold ailments of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who cure themselves with it often become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to put the cup a little lower by the place of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The poultice on the neck is in place of the salve for the head and the brain, and therefore it is worth for the constriction of the breast.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for rupture of the channel of the womb, and for the swelling, and for inflation.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to press a little harder, because if it holds too tightly, it causes forgetfulness of the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The poultices on the two sides of the neck are worth for the pains of the head, and ophthalmia and headache, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of the salve for the brain; and you must command the servant to express his hand gently when applying it, so that he does not pinch the artery or take excessive blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The poultices under the chin are worth for mouth diseases, and for gum corruption, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the salves for the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The poultices on the shoulders are worth for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The poultices on the sides are worth as much as those of three wounds of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because they drain blood from these large wounds;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the servant not to probe too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh and close to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The poultice on the backside is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and diseases beneath, and it must be large and made of lead, so that it can draw out well. And maybe, if it were too fine, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The poultices on the legs are very effective in drawing out blood from all over the body and are worth for old pains of the kidneys, bladder, and bowels, and they also relieve swellings; and they take the place of two sores on the feet, and two ankle sores. And, furthermore, they weaken the body after a long use, and bring on palpitations in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the poultice is as follows: first place it empty and let the sweat temper it, then apply it immediately, and move it equally in all directions, and do not stop doing this until you see the area become red and inflamed, and appear with a reddish color of blood; then probe and reapply the poultices, and be aware of the condition of the body, for there are some who have tough flesh and clear pores: it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make wide and somewhat deep wounds, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, you must strike it a third time; and when we wish to draw out blood slowly and by little bits, we only need do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to let out a lot of blood, we must do it often; and if the vein is thick, we must strike it straight in and the ends must be pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin and numerous pores that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with oil that opens up and dissolves.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is with essence, or violet oil, or oil of sweet almonds, or cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is with rue, oil of garlic, lily, chamomile, or anything similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person who is being cured has soft flesh and wide pores, there should not be put any oil in it.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it should be washed after the cupping with red water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or anything similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the person who has a lot of moisture should rise from ash, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities rise from old wine, or water of sage, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to cure with cupping in front of the bath or during the bath, but rather an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after being cupped.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary to be careful about when he must be cupped and how long the cups are left on.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who cure themselves if they are choleric, and if the disease is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so he should take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce with vinegar, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and melons, and horse meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup and medium wine that is between old and new, and melon, and melon, and small birds such as pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men at times treacle or musk before the cupping, or after, in order to comfort the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and the treatment should be subtle with the disease, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cups that are put on the places where it hurts to be pricked are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the groin and the thighs, because those members do not bear to be pricked there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and they are made only in order to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as we put on the shoulders when the blood is stagnated there, in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put cups on the belly and on the groin to diminish the size of the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain when there is swelling or abscess, and by its attractive virtue it happens to remove the swelling, or draw out the abscess from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way it does when it is put on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained windiness.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cups are administered empty to suck only, and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of boiling water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in diseases of the eye-socket, and in this way one fills the cup with hot water only, or with water in which herbs have been cooked that are useful for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cup administered to fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has 2 thumbs of length and half a palm in depth, and on the edge around the middle one small perforation, just like to pierce an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be of lead, soft so that it does not hurt the patient when put on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle a cross-shaped rod of lead or iron to hold a candle in place.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there are great and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the cups for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this cup in this way over the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	dip the candle in wax or a thin oil, and place it inside the cup across the rod that is inside the cup.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the cup, so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and the handles should be above the perforation that we said of, so that when one wants, the steam will go out, and take away the cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and anoint with oil just as before, and repeat often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cup administered for disease of the eye-socket, with all water, there is no rod or perforation, and it is not administered but when it is full of water, and is placed on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	And these cups are not administered except in members where one cannot put cups because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare places of fat, such as the navel or shoulders, and other similar ones.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find cups that are in sweet clean water without any imperfection, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put one nut in sweet water, until they become familiar and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed with wine and cupping, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the cups.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and cheerful, if that is a place where one can put a cup, then put it there, because it will be very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place with a needle, and then with a knife, very well, and then clean it out.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place is too sore after the body of the cups, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and put it on, until the cup is tightened.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the cup is multiplied, put on vinegar that has been boiled, or gallnuts, and similar things, until it is tightened.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put on the place half of peeled beans and leave them there until they are burnt to the flesh, it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other cups.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the cups do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the cup comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are burning, sprinkle on a little alum and burnt silk or ash, so they will be cheerful now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the Book of Burns.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and are a remedy for burns and scalds.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen, dear son, that the foolish fool is falling from this chapter, which they never saw in any of the ancient books nor read a letter of.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is the knowledge strange in our land, for I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have dealt with the science and through experience, and through the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have clearly described in this chapter what is contained and abbreviated at the end, and shown the clear forms of instruments that are administered, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the prologue of this book, the summaries of which and the chapters wise men put their understanding and remain on virtue, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when burn or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient first from one part and then from another, unless some other thing takes priority, such as weakness of body, or fever, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the patient's blood is too cold, or too hot; and in particular, if he has cold choler, meaning cold juices, and flesh of hare and kid, and does not drink wine, nor eat greasy meats, and does not fill himself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt of warm aposteme or spreading of matter to the member; then revive the patient with their first proper government as they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to recover, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meats that make thick nourishment or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and kidneys, and livers, and pig's trotters, and beef stomach, and oysters, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the bones mend more quickly and the break recovers sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old people and those who are decrepit cannot mend well nor heal according to their nature due to the scorching of the members, nor those that are too fragile, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, scrape over the broken bone a thick layer of gristle that hardens and joins the member together, so that it strengthens itself just as before; and do not remove its work, and because of this it needs to be nourished with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the back or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the bone, and others that break in splintering, such as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small fissure throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own method, and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the recollection comes to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the break of a bone by what the place is twisted and well opened from outside, and sounds when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have a twist, fissure, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you must not move it with the hand, but put on remedies that come later, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that goes to the bone and separates the two parts, you must now put them back in equal point, so that warm apostemes may come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if warm apostemes come, let it be left alone a day, until the apostemes are calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it back in its place with a slight and gentle movement, and know that the restoration of the bone is easier than the restorations of those who have splintered parts; then bind it, as it should be later on.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are splintered pieces, and they extend from two parts, then it is hands or feet, or to your hand, if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member back according to its natural figure, so that when the splintered parts of the member are loosened, scrape off by all means the additions in their places with a gentle touch, and take care that through your work no harm or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join the two ends of the bones together well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if you feel that it is not well, test it with your hand, and straighten it beautifully, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it as those who through their work cause warm aposteme and contraction in the member, as we have often said.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, scold the patient well so that they do not move it, nor while watching, sleeping, turning, or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is so secure that the patient feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it does not feel any pain, then it is not in place, and it needs to be put back into such a condition that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is placed correctly, so that twisting does not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as wrists and elbows and similar ones: it is necessary to envelop them with soft and subtle linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to envelop them with a wide and strong linen cloth, because the wide linens embrace all the great member and bind it from all parts equally, so that there is no looseness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie entwined straps lightly, three turns or four according to the member, and bind your hand with a little piece to the whole cloth, then go up above the break and bind it less tightly, so that the break is not too far apart.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen cloth little by little, as much as you take a healthy part of the place, then take another strip and tie it around again on the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and bind it moderately, not too tight nor too loosely, as we said in the first layer above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the linen strips or cloths, as long as it is all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made bandages on top, if there is no aposteme or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or aposteme, then put on something that calms the warm aposteme and removes the swelling, and let it be for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind above your bandages, and let them be as wide as a half of a cane's thickness, or made from wood like the ones used for knives, or from palm branches, and let them be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the bandage put on the break is a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it needs to be for the member's smallness or largeness.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind above the bandages in the same way as you did at the first layer, then tie on top with a string in an even manner, just like at the first layer above the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is on top, the looser; and it must be that the string is moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the strings are too thick, like those I have seen in the works of fools who make their bandages with twisted linen cords, and it is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it must not have between each bandage less than two finger widths of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the edges of the bandages after being tied up in their healthy places, then put underneath them strips of linen or ragged flannel, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the skin is torn, I will say the treatment later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind bandages to all broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it is not necessary to put bandages on it before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your security from warm aposteme supervening.
