And the restoration is thus: one puts back what was out of place on its hinges as long as it can be assembled; then put the splint, and if you need to, put an iron rod round it, and bind it so as it should be; then replace all the settings that we have said for other breaks, such as applying heat and similar remedies; and apply whatever is needed for each accident until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right name "ulna", and the other is called "fibula"; and it has every other breakage like it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is similarly as that of the arm equally, and the work is all alike.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then turns the leg completely out of shape.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone (fibula) is broken, it turns outward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the thick bone (ulna) is broken, one feels great pain and it's visible; and it turns downwards. Then apply extension, and put it back in place, and tie the splints equally; but nonetheless, it's necessary that if the break is ugly and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and more lightweight; and make it lighter according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two wooden splints that fit the leg on one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to below it. Then wrap them in two layers with a bandage above and below, and tie them together in the middle; and at this point the leg will not be able to move to the right or left, and thus it is well. And some give one strip of wood, long as the leg, and made of wood, and place it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly make up what is lacking in the break where there is an open wound; and every day stir the leg around to see if there is any hot swelling or other accident; and take care of it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of the bones of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle there does not come a break, but to the two bones of the foot sometimes comes a break and the small toe, and there is no fault that does more harm in other arrangements.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there has been a break in the two bones of the foot and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put such patients on their feet on the earth, just like they would go, and then place your own foot over theirs, at the spot where the bones are raised, then press them so hard that they return to their places; then apply the splint and bind it with cloth, and place under the lower part of the foot a small table, two inches thick, then tighten the splint onto the foot slowly, then once you have wrapped the bandages around and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, then loosen the bandage, for you will find that the bones are aligned, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some toes broken, then put them back in place, just as we have said to put the toes of the hand back in place. Then place a splint on the broken toe according to its length and be a little wider, then place under the foot that table I mentioned, and tighten it slowly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped up in one cloth of linen, and strain the table under the foot; and so as they should be on top of the end of the table out from under the lower part of the foot, that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget to remember the other things that I have said about other breakings, since we have discussed them; and treat each injury according to its needs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Une autre partie du texte !
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, then make her sit and enlarge herself, then incline her to the part of the back and be held from behind; then fill the natural cavity with cotton and put as much in it as .i. stone; then let the woman down and lift the back little by little, and then the cotton will burst so that it comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns the bone with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, then remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in and do this for seven days or around: then the breakage will be restored and if you see it, take a bladder of thistle and tie it to the navel with a cord, and put the whole bladder into the natural cavity; then blow into the cord firmly so that the bladder is inflated inside: the nature will return to its original position; then fill it with cotton and leave it for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the heel of man or woman is broken, then restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the thigh; and these recent breakages are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice into it and listens to my book. For the breakage signifies the right way of restoration in many dispositions: listen to this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap a cloth around it and leave it for three days or near that: and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Je vois que nous avons changé de sujet !
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the person who has a break with a wound, just as great as the bones of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be cured now, so that the stitches we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals but becomes infected with vitriol, and you don't have anything else, then start restoring the break again at the same hour or on the same day, lest abscesses form and it doesn't come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come out, then leave the restoration just until the ninth day, so that the abscess is quieted, and don't touch it on the third day or on the quarter, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on top of the skin uncovered, it is necessary that you put it in a gentle point to your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not ready for you to put it evenly on your hands, then make the instrument which is made of iron, which has 7 or 8 inches long, and its width according to the quantity of the wound; and so it is necessary that the craftsman take 3 or 4, according to what he needs in each cure of a break; and let it be rounded and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend at the compression on the member under your work, and be angled forward, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved nails should be placed on top of the visible bone; and screw them in once, so that they turn back, and be even with one another. And if the break is fine, and the instrument cannot well take hold of the bone, then you must saw off the top of the bone, until the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot restore the bone to its place, as we have said, then take a suitable instrument, such as an awl or gouge, and scrape out what remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is restored, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Do this until it is in its place, then soak one cloth in black vinegar, and properly clean it; and do not put cerate or another ointment on the wound that has oil, lest it cause infection and corruption; then administer medicines once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and sew a covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted with the breakage; and many times this has been done by foolish men, and they have caused death or corruption on the patient one time or another; and the constriction is softer and more pleasant than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that bad accidents may come from it, as we have said, and you feel pain at the site, then do not put salves on it; but enfold around it, in place of salves, hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one day or two bowels coming to the wound, then take off what you have put on top with vinegar, and put healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmac's ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the member two times a day, in the morning and at nightfall, until it is solidified and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be aligned in such a way that the bowels go down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it passes many days and cannot heal but rather the bowels keep coming out, know that there are small pieces of bone in it, for which reason you should sew up the wound with a thread, and take out all these loose fragments that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if an abscess or any other kind of corruption comes to the wound, you should treat it according to what he says in his previous chapter. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the member, such as the shinbone or the ulna, and others similar to the large members, do not extract it, because many times it becomes dead flesh; but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come on top of the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come back many times after the healing of the bruise, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and perhaps the member cannot do its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, take care if the swelling is fresh: administer medicinal purges, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, aloe vera, and similar others, in the same way that you would take any of these things or all of them together, and mix them with purgative vinegar or with beaten egg or with oil; and apply them to the wound with a compress, and bind it tightly, and do not loosen it for a day; then loosen it, and start again another one, as long as the swelling is gone; or you strain over a well-made cloth; because the properties of cloth are that they remove all the swellings on the members; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then cut off the excess above it, or have it shaved by a barber until it is gone, and cure it once it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and after it remains weak and fragile in the member, it happens for many causes: one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or because of excessive bruising; or due to very great movements, not at its own time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make the body tender, until the blood is multiplied in it; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and cheerfulness; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and often soak with hot water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and restore it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the deformed limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that you should break the limb all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great harm, and perhaps death. However, if the swelling and torture are fresh, it is necessary to soak them with hot water, or cook soothing herbs, such as valerian leaves, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a soft plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of valerian, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take fatty figs, and grind them with linseed meal, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at any time the swelling is removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with damp hands, and movement is administered to the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting has turned into a hardened and calcified state, like stone, and it needs to be cut out with a scalpel, then cover just up to the bone, cutting carefully and lightly with a fine edge; and apply cauterization and a poultice in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of Dislocations (or Fractures)
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	A dislocation is a displacement of some joint from its place, because it cannot move, and the member is badly shaped, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes to someone, it is necessary to reduce it immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the joint becomes inflamed, and perhaps it is set into place with pain in the joint. Therefore, one should not move it to its normal place while it is inflamed: many times this brings on spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when this happens, one makes the patient rest until the swelling has gone down; then they soak the member in hot water and oil, then gently rub it with a linen cloth, and treat each joint as its cure comes into place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of Dislocations from the top of the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones (or mandibles)
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Something happens when the jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both jaws is in two ways: or they are slightly displaced from their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the breast, and cut off the saliva from the mouth that it can't hold, nor close its mouth, and enclose its tongue with the words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in a few dispositions (or without much trouble).
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you must rub it quickly, and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in such a way that the ministrant (or treating physician) holds the patient's head, and inserts the mirror's soft pouch from one of his hands into the root of the jawbone's dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and with the other two hands, he should support it equally; and command the patient to soften and move their jaws in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the ministrant makes it even, so that it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reduction is difficult, or even if it's both jawbones together, you should soak them in hot water and oil, until they are softened slightly; nor delay the reduction, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reduced equally and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, then put a moist cloth on it made from rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with soft ligatures.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on their back, and their jaws should be supported between two pillows, so that they do not move to either side, nor try to open them, but rather take soft food, until the pain is gone and the jawbones are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then gradually eat whatever they want lightly, and do not exert themselves to open their mouth to eat or drink, until the jawbones are well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not converted back to their usual state, then fever and severe pain ensue, and perhaps belly cramps, and possibly vomiting of cold, clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a mortal condition; and many times the person who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the elbow (or forelle)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The elbow cannot be dislocated from the side towards the spine in its continuation, and it is always dislocated to the outside, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the reduction is that the patient lies down on their back and stretches out their arms; then presses the dislocated joint firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place; then put on a poultice and bandage, and tighten it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the joint that is towards the shoulder cannot be dislocated; if it is not, and if it does become dislocated, then you should reduce it to its place, as we have said; then put on a poultice and bandage, and tighten it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly, the shoulder joint is reduced when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the Dislocation of the Shoulder (or Spaulle)
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: first, it dislocates towards the armpit below; second, it dislocates towards the spine; and possibly it dislocates upwards, which happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate downwards for the nerves; and more often it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for theirs comes out quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it goes back with pain, and returns with pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that they are percussed or crushed, and the shoulder becomes inflamed with a hot swelling, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must examine it carefully, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it is downwards towards the armpit, and you will find a clear distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the armpit on the other side, the top of the shoulder, just like an empty space; and the patient cannot return their hand to its normal place, nor move it with any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly on the outside.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to reduce when it is new or if the infant is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the ministrant lifts the patient's hand up high, then puts their thumbs under the armpit, and lifts the joint with force up to its place; and the ministrant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back in; and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back as we have said after several days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the ministrant should apply a soothing and calming poultice, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilotus in water, and have them administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then have the patient lie on their back, and put a linen cloth of equal thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, under the armpit, then place the ministrant's heel on top of it, and lift the shoulder joint virtuously, and draw the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another ministrant holds the patient's head, so that it does not move down; and the shoulder returns immediately, and if you see that it reduces in this manner, then...
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and that you have present a man who is larger than the patient, and stands directly beside them, and puts their shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lifts the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in it.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another ministrant pulls the patient's hand down towards their stomach. And if the patient is too light, they can hold with them something heavy, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is also reduced in another manner: and that one puts a long wooden skewer into the ground, whose length is as long as a fist, and neither too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	and it is placed under the patient, but with a soft cloth over it, and the patient's hand is extended downwards on the other side forcefully, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return through all the things that we have said, then do this cure: take a skewer of two arms in length and four fingers in width, whose head is rounded to fit easily into the depth under the armpit, in this shape...
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a cloth over the top of the skewer so that the skewer does not hurt the patient, then place it under the armpit of the patient; and extend your arm over the length of the skewer, and tie the elbow on top of the skewer, and the arm at the hand, then place the arm over a wooden splint of one and a half fingers in width, and have the hands extended downwards, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however it may be, then you should put under the armpit a linen ball of equal size, then apply an ointment made with flour powder, incense and egg fat, over the entire shoulder and around it; then tighten the bandage under the armpit gently, and turn the cloth over the ointment, and bind the hand to the neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat lightly, until the members are comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and then eat again in 5 or 7 days, and move him; and if it is firm and has not softened, it means it is sound.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is not yet in its proper place, or because of moisture that it has come to, or for another reason, then you should administer cauterization at three small punctures, as if they were placed before a cauterizer's needle.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and after 7 days, the joint still does not hold and cannot lift their arm up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs towards the spine, and shoulders, or back, is caused by a blow, and stretching of the hands, and it administers another type of injury; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the member and delay in movement, then have the patient bathe many times until the stiffness is alleviated and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the Dislocation of the Shoulder (or Coute)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in parts, and returns to its place in parts; and it is dislocated from all sides, and also before and behind, and the dislocation is not easily reduced, because one can see it well and feel it well; and it occurs according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you bring the sick shoulder together with the healthy one, you can see it clearly apart. For the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its own shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reduce it in such a way that hot swellings come, because if hot swellings come, it will be more painful to reduce; and perhaps it cannot be fully reduced at all, especially when it occurs behind; then it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death ensues.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is such that when it can be reduced, you should extend their hand with your two hands; and their arms should be stretched out, and the ministrant's hands around the shoulder joint, on top of it and underneath, and push the joint into its own place, or to the root of their palm, until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when they bring their hand to their own hand, and firmly press the root of the palm on the shoulder that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and have two ministrants stretch out the arm, and tie them together with a cloth, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from each side, then take a double long and wide cloth...
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the ministrant has joined the joint to their hand, they should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly, until it returns to its place.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is back in place, they should put on dry ointment with egg fat, and the bandage firmly, and bind the arm to the neck of the patient, and let it be for some time, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the poultice and the ligament, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels grief after the dislocated joint is reset, and it swells, then bathe him and rub gently, and press until it is eased; or put a thick sheep's fat poultice on the joint, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put the poultice back on, and then have him enter the bath; and do this twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you see that it does not come back to its place, then put moist warm wadding of marsh grass on it, and bind it tight; it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return to place is slighter than that of other joints Nevertheless, it must be put back in place hastily, in the same manner as it was dislocated, even if the place swells or becomes inflamed with a hot aposteme.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the putting back in place is that you put the ailing hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the hand, and have the physician look at it equally, so that he puts his palm over the appearance of the jointure, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, you must make sure that it is properly in place; then have the physician look at it again; then put the ailing hand on its back over a table for stretching and putting back into place.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then have the ailing person put their back on the table, and have the physician put his hand over the appearance of the joint; if it goes back into place now, it's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then apply a binding of soothing ointments and hot compresses, and leave it in that way without reattempting to put it back into place.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put it back in place after any days, then the twisted joint will remain.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and nothing hurts the ailing person more than having to wait until the hand is swollen, and being unable to grasp or do anything; then know that the nerves are crushed, or the arteries have been severed; if there's no other cause for this besides being able to strain by applying cautery near the place, and perhaps it's not worth trying anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the ointment that we have mentioned, then bind and leave it for 5 days, then remove the binding and let it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then wet the hand with hot water and rub it gently until it is warmed up.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	the dislocation of the wrist
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At times they are dislocated in front of the hand on both sides, at other times in back of the palm or towards the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then place the wrist and push the dislocation into the hollows until it returns to its proper place, then hold the head of the wrist and pull it towards the part where it was disjointed.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and let it be for 2 days, then place it in its original position that day, and do not bind it, but instead leave it loose, and when you are through with the binding, as we have said, and the binding is removed, make him move his wrist, and rebind it lightly; and do this often until it is straight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same thing if it is dislocated towards the belly of the hand, and do it in the same way that you have done before, until he is healed; and do the same thing when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the spine (or more specifically, the vertebrae) at the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several that are dislocated, then there is no treatment, for death hastens the ailing person.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j. des dislocations de la hainche	of the thigh dislocations.

Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wants to restore it, there is often that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you're not wise in the art and you haven't used it for a long time, and if you're not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor too quick.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at first soothing poultices and hot compresses, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you don't see hope of healing.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then clean the member now to its place, so that the hot abscess comes.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is back to its place, then administer soothing poultices and hot compresses, and heal the wound with drying ointments as is fitting.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is breaking and small bones splintered, then set the bones, and do what we have said about simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and take heed not to fall into the way of fear, according to what I have said, because this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of arming yourself and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the treatise on medicine (Physique).
